Guangdong Province 62

Agricultural Product Inspection Fee Controversy

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the Guangzhou Agricultural Product Pest Inspection Office of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining began inspections on the 10th of this month, it has started by detaining goods from seafood merchants and ordering them to pay fees. The Guangzhou General Chamber of Commerce sent representatives to the office to negotiate, requesting the release of the goods and a one-week delay. The chamber convened a meeting of seafood merchants and other related merchants on the 18th to discuss the matter, inviting representatives from the office to explain. The office director, Yao Xinghuang, agreed to this. However, various seafood merchants, fearing further detentions as goods continued to arrive from other provinces before the fundamental issue was resolved, wired Hong Kong to halt shipments. Even those already loaded onto ships and arriving in the provincial river were returned to Hong Kong pending resolution.

Yesterday, the 18th, at 3 PM, the Guangzhou General Chamber of Commerce convened a special meeting. Over sixty committee members attended. Huang Jifang from the Guangzhou Agricultural Product Inspection Office and representatives from the municipal party department, Zao Xing, and from the dried fruit and seafood merchant guilds, Liang Ziguang, Yi Zichang, He Hanxuan, Guan Yueshan, Zhu Qiulun, Zhu Ruzhen, and Zhu Shaoming, were present. Yuan Ciming, the chairman, opened the meeting with a formal address, explaining the reason for the meeting. He then invited Huang Jifang, the representative from the Agricultural Product Inspection Office, to explain. Huang stood up and stated that his mission in representing the Agricultural Product Inspection Office was to clarify merchants' misunderstandings about agricultural product inspection. Its purpose can be divided into two aspects: first, to secure equal international trade status for our domestic agricultural products; and second, to prevent the invasion of foreign agricultural product pests. As for the merchants' reporting procedures, they will be made as simple as possible. Agricultural product inspection is a new undertaking in China. Advanced countries in Europe and America have been doing this for a long time. Chinese agricultural products shipped abroad have been repeatedly detained or denied entry entirely because our country lacks agricultural product inspection certificates, preventing us from obtaining equal international trade status. Therefore, to enhance the status of Chinese agricultural products, it is necessary to conduct pest inspections. This also serves to prevent foreign goods with pests from entering. As for the inspection fee, charging one percent of the value is approved by the Executive Yuan, which is significantly less than the twenty percent charged in foreign countries. The procedure is also extremely simple. Hong Kong is a hub for the import of foreign agricultural products. Therefore, to facilitate reporting for various merchants, the office has entrusted the Hong Kong China Xunzheng Company (4th floor of the Hong Kong Trading Building) to handle pest inspection matters according to regulations. All general merchants importing seeds, seedlings, fruits, and aquatic products from abroad must promptly report to this company for inspection and obtain inspection certificates and permits before the goods are distributed to various sub-merchants. Otherwise, the goods will be detained and penalized when transported to the mainland. He hoped that merchants in the city would notify the Hong Kong General Chamber of Commerce to report and obtain certificates in accordance with this, ensuring smooth transactions. Next, a representative from the seafood merchant guild stated that the government's implementation of agricultural product inspection is a policy to protect agriculture and prevent the invasion of foreign agricultural product pests, which is justified. However, the various merchant guilds have been burdened with heavy taxes and levies in recent years and cannot afford the inspection fees. Moreover, charging one percent of the value is simply unaffordable. Furthermore, the regulations mention inspecting fruits, seeds, seedlings, and aquatic products for pests, but Chinese seafood products are numerous and mostly come to the province from Hong Kong due to distance. If domestic products also need to be inspected, it will be unbearable and inconsistent with the purpose of preventing foreign goods with pests. In addition, the inspection period extends from three days to twenty days. Seafood cannot be delayed, and the losses would be incalculable. Moreover, aquatic products are not within the scope of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining. If inspection is required, it should be handled by the Ministry of Health. Therefore, the guild believes it cannot comply and requests a delay to protect commerce. The inspection office representative reiterated that the inspection time is not a problem, having already explained that the fee is collected and the inspection done in Hong Kong. Once an inspection certificate and permit are obtained, the procedure is complete. When the goods arrive in the province, simply submit the certificate to the office on Guanglou, Changdi, to pick up the goods. As for the request for a delay, it is beyond his authority to answer. The allocation of aquatic products to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining is an administrative matter, and the Executive Yuan has its reasons for assigning it to that ministry. Next, Li Zhuoyu, a member of the Chamber of Commerce, stated that since the inspection office representative has no authority to respond to the points raised by the seafood merchant representative, the seafood merchants and other related merchants should submit their difficulties and reasons for non-compliance in writing to the chamber, which will forward them to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining for consideration. The municipal agricultural product inspection office should delay implementation pending resolution. Next, Zhao Jingru, a member of the Chamber of Commerce, stated that the inspection office representative said that reporting and paying fees through the Hong Kong General Chamber of Commerce would allow goods to be transported to the mainland. He believed that this was inconsistent with the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining's purpose of inspecting for pests and was primarily aimed at collecting fees, as goods can be transported to the mainland as long as the fee is paid and a certificate is obtained. Furthermore, many domestic agricultural products are transported to the province from Hong Kong. The inspection office staff must have considerable expertise in identifying and testing pests, but whether they can accurately distinguish between domestic and foreign agricultural products without error is questionable. For example, squid produced in Beihai, Xiamen, and Qingdao are domestic products, while those produced in Japan are foreign goods. Can the inspectors distinguish them without error or delay? Also, it must be explained whether the inspection standards are limited to the items listed on the list, permanently valid, and without changes. The inspection office representative replied that the office has specialized testing personnel for pest inspection and is continuing to hire more. The inspection standards are, of course, based on the list and are permanently valid. However, similar items still need to be inspected and fees charged, while dissimilar items may be exempt. Next, Peng Chuli, a member of the Chamber of Commerce, stated that agricultural products are needed by the people, and charging one percent of the value has a significant impact on the national economy. Preventing the entry of foreign agricultural products is a customs policy and not the responsibility of the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining. Since the inspection office representative cannot be responsible for answering, a delay should be requested first, and the various merchants should submit their opinions to the chamber, which will directly forward them to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to strive for discussion. At this point, the inspection office representative stopped responding, stating that the explanation task was complete and no further discussion was needed. Chamber of Commerce representatives Jiang Zhongya and Huang Yongyu then expressed their hope that the inspection office representative would report the opinions of the various merchants to the director for improvement to achieve mutual benefit and instructed the various merchants to submit their difficulties in writing to the chamber for forwarding to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining to strive for change. Next, a representative from the tobacco merchant guild raised a question, requesting the inspection office representative to answer on the spot, asking whether tobacco is subject to inspection as it is listed in the regulations but not on the list. The inspection office representative replied that although tobacco is listed in the regulations, it has not been determined by the Executive Yuan and is temporarily not subject to inspection. The meeting then adjourned.

Gaomi: Japanese Merchants Selling Narcotics 63

Jinan Correspondence: The Civil Affairs Department previously received an order from the Shandong Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee, forwarding a request from the Gaomi County Party Department to devise a method to prohibit Japanese merchants from selling narcotics and transporting firearms. The department instructed strict prohibition. The county magistrate of Gaomi, Miao Dingbao, reported back, stating that there are nine foreign firms established by Japanese in the city, including Gongrong, Tianlong, Hanchuan, Jiushan, Meida, Longchang, Sanda, Jinkang, and Jincheng. The county magistrate had heard of their improper conduct soon after arriving. He immediately ordered the police to closely monitor and strictly prohibit their activities. He also summoned various landlords to inquire about the details. They all claimed that the Japanese were openly using the buildings as foreign firms but secretly selling narcotics, poisoning the people and bullying them. They requested prompt negotiations to order them to vacate the premises in order to maintain sovereignty. Attached was a survey of the addresses of the Japanese firms and the original submissions from various landlords requesting submission of the matter for negotiation. The county magistrate had personally negotiated with the Japanese, but they relied on their power and refused to reason. The magistrate was unable to resort to violent measures. The Civil Affairs Department noted that since Gaomi County is not a treaty port, the unauthorized residence of Japanese merchants and their occupation of civilian houses to sell narcotics violated international conventions. The county magistrate was specifically ordered that, according to the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty, Japanese subjects are allowed to reside and trade in China only at treaty ports. When traveling inland, they must obtain a license from their consulate and submit it to the Chinese local government for stamping. When passing through places, they must present the license for verification before being allowed to proceed. If no license is found or if there is illegal activity, they should be sent to the consulate for punishment. Along the way, they can only be detained, not abused. Since Gaomi County is not a treaty port, the Japanese merchants are audaciously residing there without authorization and occupying civilian houses to sell narcotics, which is a violation of the treaty and laws. In addition to requesting the provincial government to seriously negotiate with the consul, asking him to do his utmost to stop the Japanese people from engaging in such illegal activities again, the county magistrate was ordered to immediately select police officers to detain the illegal Japanese merchants and hand them over to the consul along with the evidence, providing documents nearby, punishing them, and only restricting their freedom along the way, without abuse. All houses should be returned to the original owners, and the detailed handling should be reported. The provincial government had already been requested to seriously negotiate with the Japanese consul.

Harbin Municipal Council Ordered to Reorganize 64

Harbin Correspondence: Regarding the reorganization of the Harbin Municipal Council, the Governor-General's Office has today ordered the Special Municipal Bureau and the Municipal Self-Government Association to comply. The original order is as follows: [The third re-election of the Harbin Municipal Self-Government Association has caused disputes and lawsuits, which have continued for nearly two months without resolution. The Governor-General's Office has reviewed the points of dispute and, according to the old regulations, finds it difficult to cope, losing both legal and factual grounds. When the Governor-General took office in the 17th year, the second re-election had not yet been completed, and there were various disputes at that time. It was already recognized that many of these regulations should be amended. However, due to the outbreak of the Sino-Russian incident in the middle of last year and the instability of the region, it was not desirable to make changes rashly. Now that the old case has just been settled, a new wave has arisen. Upon weighing the situation, it is believed that there is no other way but to reform. The Governor-General's Office has listed in detail the shortcomings and incompleteness of the regulations and the various facts of this dispute and proposes to suspend the meeting for three months to quickly amend the regulations. During this suspension period, all matters to be handled by the Special Municipal Bureau should be submitted to the Governor-General's Office for approval. Once the new regulations are approved and promulgated, the Self-Government Association should be established in accordance with the regulations and then submit the documents to the bureau for approval. The Northeast Political Affairs Committee instructed that the above issues were presented to the Northeast Political Affairs Committee. The instructions stated that the fundamental cause of this dispute is the incompleteness of the Self-Government Trial Regulations and the failure to establish election and deliberation rules. If they are not fundamentally clarified and redefined, the dispute cannot be resolved. The Governor-General should, in accordance with the National Government's previously promulgated Special Municipal Organization Law, and considering the special circumstances of the region, quickly draft the above regulations and submit them for approval and implementation. Before approval, all matters stipulated in Article 21 of the original Trial Regulations should be temporarily reported by the Municipal Bureau to the Governor-General's Office for approval. Therefore, it should be complied with. In addition to issuing orders for compliance and waiting for the new regulations to be submitted for approval, the bureau and the association are hereby ordered to comply.]

Soviet Russia's Plot to Redden Northern Manchuria 65

Three Steps

With a Five-Year Plan

Harbin Correspondence: Since the Eastern Railway was restored to its original state, the Soviet Union

Page 10

has determined to redden northern Manchuria. The first step is to replace the Russian employees of the Eastern Railway with Soviet personnel who are all party members. Although the power originally held by the director of the Eastern Railway is easy to handle, there are various difficulties. The second step is to use the principle of being close to the ink and the source to redden the Chinese employees with Soviet employees. Although it is slightly more difficult, it will gradually be contaminated and eroded over time. Eventually, it will be achieved, and they will be made to enter the scope of reddening without realizing it. The third step is to have the Eastern Railway employees responsible for expanding propaganda, spreading the red ideology to outside workers, northern Manchurian farmers, and even the proletariat. This is the Soviet Union's great plot after regaining control of the Eastern Railway. It is stipulated that the implementation period is five years, and the director, deputy director, and various department heads of the Eastern Railway, as well as the leaders of each station along the line and the foremen, are responsible for carrying out the plan. The first step is for one year, and the second and third steps are both for two years. According to foreign reports, Director Ludyi recently visited various stations on the east, west, and south lines with the various department heads and secretaries of the railway for inspection. Although it is a routine matter after taking office, the mission he carries is to prepare for the implementation of the first and second steps, instructing the leaders of each station to proceed according to the predetermined plan, depending on the situation, and stipulating rewards and punishments. If significant results are not achieved in the next six months, the responsible leaders will be recorded with demerits and have their salaries deducted. If there are still no results within a year and a half, the responsible leaders will be dismissed and sent back to Moscow for punishment. Conversely, if a certain degree of success is achieved or exceeded within the stipulated period, they will be rewarded or have their salaries increased and promoted. The regulations are very detailed and are generally entrusted to Communist Party Russian members for implementation. All Soviet nationals who are not Communist Party members are not allowed to participate. This is the preparation for the second step. As for the third step, Director Ludyi and Deputy Director Danisov are responsible for carrying it out. The plan is to first dismiss all stateless Russian personnel inside and outside the bureau, and the remaining positions will be completely filled by Soviet Communist Party members. At the beginning of this month, more than eighty of these stateless Russian personnel have been dismissed. The stateless Russian personnel in the railway who have not been dismissed are also afraid that they will not be able to remain in their positions for long. Therefore, they jointly submitted a petition to the Soviet Consulate General in Harbin, which was forwarded to the Soviet government, requesting to join the Soviet nationality in order to preserve their jobs. However, the Soviet government believed that they were speculators with cunning intentions and immediately telegraphed Mei Melnikov, the Consul General in Harbin, ordering him not to allow them to join the nationality and to telegraph Director Lu of the Eastern Railway to dismiss them all. Although the name is to hate their speculation, in fact, they took this opportunity to implement the first step of the reddening of the Eastern Railway plan. At present, there are still more than 300 stateless employees in the Eastern Railway, all of whom are special technicians.

Director Lu had previously sent telegrams to various railways in the Soviet Union to select railway workers who were party members to come to Harbin. When these employees arrive, the fate of the stateless employees is feared to be over. After clearing the stateless employees, the Soviet employees who are not Communist Party members will also be laid off separately, and the total period is completely cleared within one year, all to be replaced by Communist Party members. In addition to replacing all technical positions with ordinary railway workers who have technical skills, the rest are generally supplemented by Communist Party members with military status. This is the Soviet Union's grand conspiracy to redden the Eastern Railway and redden northern Manchuria. The first two steps have been prepared for implementation separately, and the first step is successful as the preparation for the third step. In addition, the Soviet government, in view of the fact that during the Sino-Russian Incident last autumn, most of the Soviet railway workers of the "big radish" type did not comply with the government's strike order and still lingered and refused to leave, so that the Chinese Eastern Railway continued as usual, the Soviet Union was deeply dissatisfied with these railway workers. After the restoration of the Eastern Railway in January this year, the Soviet authorities of the Eastern Railway used a broadsword to implement layoffs and to supplement the real communists one by one so that they could act together to resist us in the event of another incident. It is learned that the Russian deputy director of the Eastern Railway Health Department, formerly Shibeiberg, has been in office for more than three years, has excellent knowledge and rich experience, and recently the Soviet Union suddenly sent Ivanitsky to replace him, which is also one of his retributions.

Another meeting to publicize the method of curing rice borers will be held, and from July 1, personnel will be dispatched to Huguan, Huanghao, Mudu, Nanbeiqiao, Dongshan, and the urban area to publicize the campaign. Instructors for the rice borer control campaign in each district were also assigned.

Difficulties in Interrogation of Prisoners Transferred to Military Prison: The transfer of 30 unsentenced prisoners, including Chen Yi, Lu Yuren, and Xue Hao, from the Jiangsu Third Sub-Prison and the Gaoyuan Detention Center on Sishiqian Street to the Military Prison has aroused a reaction from the Shanghai Lawyers Association and the Wuxian Lawyers Association, which have telegraphed the Judicial Yuan, the Ministry of Justice, and the Supreme Court to dismiss and punish Ding Lei, the director of the three sub-prisons. As of yesterday (26th), the Shanghai Lawyers Association specially appointed lawyers Liu Zuwang and Yu Zonglu as representatives to visit Lin Biao, the president of the High Court in Suzhou, to inquire about the matter. The case falls under judicial secrecy and cannot be announced. Among the unsentenced prisoners who were transferred, Miao Zhuanglin and Xu Jiajin, who were involved in the anti-revolutionary case, happened to be tried by Huang Bingdao, the presiding judge of the Third Criminal Court, at 2:00 p.m. yesterday (26th). At 1:00 p.m., a ticket was signed ordering the bailiff to go to the detention center to interrogate Ding, who also served as the director of the detention center. Ding ordered the warden to bring the two prisoners to the military prison. The warden of the military prison refused to allow the interrogation because the prisoners were detained under the order of the Ministry of Military Affairs and the High Court. The prison was immediately turned over to Huang, the presiding judge of the Third Criminal Court, who stated that each case tried in court was independent and that the unsentenced prisoners were usually detained in the detention center for easy interrogation and should not be held in the military prison, which would cause a barrier. Therefore, the bailiff was ordered to go to the detention center to bring them back, but the trial was not brought back until 4:00 p.m.

Changshu 69

The Ministry of Finance Dispatches Commissioners to Withdraw 20,000 Yuan: The day before yesterday, the Ministry of Finance sent Yan Zhongfu, a native of Changshu, to Changshu to withdraw 20,000 yuan. It is said that before the Ministry of Finance sent the commissioner Yan, it ordered Magistrate Tan to check the account books after the arrival of the commissioner Yan and to withdraw all the collected funds. If the number of quotas is not met, the county magistrate should be ordered to find other ways to raise funds.

Meeting on Grain Price Stabilization: Magistrate Tan has commissioned Xu Jingxi, chairman of the County Chamber of Commerce, to purchase 2,000 bags of foreign rice in Shanghai to stabilize the grain price in the county. The county government submitted five measures to the district chief's meeting on the 24th: (1) Hengtang and Hongdou districts should be used as disaster areas to investigate the farmers and poor people. The disaster area is based on ten mu as the standard, and hawkers are all regarded as poor households (1) The investigation of poor households must be completed in all districts before July 10 (1) The stabilized grain price is based on the original purchase price, and the shortage of two yuan per stone will be written off.

Wuxi 70

The Kidnapping Case in Yixing is Solved in Wuxi: Shi Dancheng's family, residents of Guan Village Township, Yixing, were kidnapped for ransom in February of last year. On the evening of the 23rd of this month, eight kidnappers suddenly came again, beating Shi Dancheng's wife, Zhang, and his younger brother, Danqu, causing injuries. Shi Dancheng's son, Shi Lin'nan, and his cousin, Shi Keshou, were kidnapped. Shi Danqu, who was injured by the bandits, took the Yongxing small steamer from Yixing to Wuxi yesterday morning, intending to seek treatment at the Bingren Hospital. At half past noon, the Yongxing steamer arrived near Luoshe in this county. Shi Danqu glimpsed a bandit ship moored there from the steamer's window. The kidnappers and hostages Shi Lin'nan and Shi Keshou were all on the ship. Danqu immediately shouted, "Lin'nan!" "Keshou!" At that time, more than ten military policemen on the same boat, upon learning the truth, immediately loaded their guns and ordered the steamer's driver to approach the bandit ship to carry out the capture. As a result, they captured one kidnapper, Sun Liubao, and rescued the two hostages, Shi Lin'nan and Shi Keshou. The remaining kidnappers escaped by swimming. One suspect, Zhou Renyun, was also arrested. The steamer then set sail for Wuxi. The military police, together with Qian Tianxiong, the chief inspector of the Public Security Bureau who was patrolling the wharf, took the kidnapper Sun Liubao, the suspect Zhou Renyun, and the hostages Shi Lin'nan and Shi Keshou to the headquarters of the Second Regiment of Military Police. Wu Chengren, the regiment commander, in order to facilitate linguistic convenience, specifically invited Chief Inspector Qian to hold a court hearing. Sun Liubao confessed that he was from Donghenglin, Changzhou, 25 years old, and made a living by farming. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Zhou Renyun was confirmed to be a law-abiding merchant and was released on bail. Sun Liubao was detained in the regiment headquarters pending transfer to the county for legal proceedings. The injured Shi Danqu went to Puren Hospital for treatment.

The Labor Dispute at the Deda Yu Silk Factory is Resolved: It has been learned that the employees of the Deda Yu Silk Factory on Jinfeng Road, Zhoushanbang, outside Guangfu Gate in Wuxi, went on strike on the afternoon of the 21st of this month. Ye Qiaoyun and Xu Junjie, the standing members of the Silk Factory Workers' Union and the factory's branch union, respectively, considering that both sides suffered from the stalemate, specially went to Shanghai the day before yesterday with Wang Dingfa, the manager of the Deda Yu Silk Factory, and Wang Yunsheng, the work director, to intercede with General Manager Shi Xingsheng. Ye Qiaoyun and Xu Junjie agreed to instruct all workers to obey the factory's management in the future. As for those who took the lead in causing trouble this time, a thorough investigation and strict punishment should be carried out. General Manager Shi only agreed to resume work after Ye and Xu signed a written guarantee as evidence. That night, Ye Qiaoyun and others returned to Wuxi by car and immediately convened a meeting of the branch union members to report on their trip to Shanghai and urged the workers to go to the factory to work and obey the factory's management. All the workers agreed, and yesterday morning, they all went to the factory to work as usual.

Procedures for Verification and Stamping of Secondary School Graduation Certificates 72

The date of graduation ceremonies for secondary schools in this city is approaching rapidly, and there has not been enough time to verify and stamp the certificates. Recently, people have been flocking to the Municipal Education Bureau to have their certificates stamped. Photos must be affixed to the certificates, and they must be affixed with a steel stamp, along with the triangular-shaped stamps and the graduation volunteer forms. These must be submitted to the bureau for verification and issuance. The volunteer form should include the following information: (1) Full name; (2) Gender; (3) Age; (4) Native place; (5) Guardian's occupation; (6) Post-graduation aspirations, including both further education and employment; (7) Other information.

Zhang Mingci and You Shaobin Travel Abroad 76

Mr. Zhang Mingci has specialized in journalism for many years. He graduated from the Graduate School of Yenching University. Five years ago, he founded the Shaonian Ribao (Youth Daily) in Peiping, advocating just revolutionary ideas. The newspaper was forcibly shut down twice. He served as the editor-in-chief of the Simin Bao and the Liming Bao, as well as a reporter and editor for the Chinese-English Culture New Youth magazine and the Nanyang Yanjiu (Southeast Asian Studies). He has also been a teacher at Beigao, Ding, and Nan schools, as well as a tutor for Wang Yunwu's family. He has a wealth of knowledge and has made significant contributions to society, culture, and education. Recently, Nihon University specially invited him to give a lecture. The Nanyang Siang Pau and the Rangoon Daily have both invited him to be their editor-in-chief, but he has not yet accepted. He is scheduled to take the American Dollar Liner this morning at 11:00 AM, via the Philippines, to lecture in Singapore and other places and to collect materials for the Department of Arts at Jinan University. His wife, Ms. You Shaobin, is skilled in poetry and painting. She is a graduate of the National Academy of Art and will accompany him. Ms. You has created many works of art and plans to hold a non-selling exhibition in Singapore and other places.

Art Education Inspection Group to Japan 78

Departing Today on the Shanghai Maru

Carrying One Hundred Exhibition Works

The National Academy of Art of Hangzhou West Lake has been requested by the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs to organize an art education inspection group to Japan this summer vacation to study the country's art and bring the school's faculty works to hold an exhibition at the Tokyo Art Museum in Japan. The school's inspection group consists of twelve people, all of whom are faculty members. They will depart in two groups. The first group of four was originally scheduled to depart from Shanghai on June 23, but due to the complicated procedures for transporting a large number of works, the time was insufficient, and the decision was changed to depart today (June 27) on the Shanghai Maru. The second group of eight members will depart from Shanghai on July 1. The exhibition period is scheduled to begin on July 6 in Tokyo for two weeks. The head of the delegation plans to stay in Japan for four weeks. In addition to studying the country's art, they will travel to famous scenic spots.

Publication of Translated Classics 81

The Lives and Thoughts of Great Philosophers of Ancient and Modern Times

| Translated by Yang Yinhong and Yang Yinwei |

Will Durant's monumental work, "The Lives and Thoughts of Great Philosophers of Ancient and Modern Times," has been translated by the Yang Yinhong and Yang Yinwei brothers. Mr. Wu Jiehui praised it as "a marvelous book," as mentioned in the June 10th issue of this newspaper. The book has now been published. The entire book has over eight hundred pages, gold-plated hardcover, a large volume, and the actual price is four yuan (the original price is equivalent to twenty yuan in national currency). Currently, a special price is being offered at three yuan and two jiao per copy until July 15th. Mail orders are accepted, and postage is not charged. The mail order address is Yu Fengbin Medical Office, Lujia Garden, West Gate, Shanghai. The Commercial Press and major bookstores in this city and other places also sell the book (mail orders to consignment shops still require postage). Samples can be requested by mail with a four-cent stamp. It is also reported that many pre-orders have been placed for the book, and the first edition is limited, so those who wish to purchase it should do so as soon as possible.

Local News of This City

Renamed Shanghai City 88

To Be Implemented Starting July 1st

The Municipal Government issued a proclamation yesterday, which reads: "Proclamation regarding the matter of renaming: In accordance with the appointment letter from the National Government, Zhang Qun is appointed as the Mayor of Shanghai City. This is noted. Upon investigation, the city organization law has been promulgated and implemented. In accordance with Article 1 of the organization law, the city is named after its location, namely, Shanghai City. It is hereby announced that starting from July 1st, this city will be renamed Shanghai City, and the Municipal Government will be renamed Shanghai Municipal Government. All citizens are hereby notified."

Telephone Negotiations in the Foreign Concession 89

The Consular Body Will Reply This Morning

The Minister of Foreign Affairs Is Determined to Protest to the End

Chinese and Foreign Company Holds Shareholders' Meeting Today

Various Groups Warned Chinese Shareholders Yesterday

Regarding the transfer of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company to the International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation, the National Government's Ministry of Transportation is preparing to buy it back at a price. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has also issued a declaration and instructed its Shanghai office to negotiate with the Shanghai Consular Body. The Consular Body also convened a second meeting and decided that the American Consul-General and leader of the Consular Body, Cunningham, would respond. The response was signed last night and sent to the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs this morning. Chen Shiguang, director of the Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Deputy Director Liu Yunfang visited Mr. Cunningham yesterday afternoon. Cunningham's opinion is that before the National Government takes back the foreign concessions, the Municipal Council remains the administrative organ of the concessions. The telephone issue in the concessions will be decided by the two Municipal Councils and ultimately by the shareholders of the telephone company. Directors Chen and Liu will present the results of the negotiations to Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting. Minister Wang's intention is to protest to the end regardless of the outcome of the telephone company's shareholders' meeting. Chen and Liu also submitted a memorandum to Minister Wang on this issue, advocating that a committee composed of both the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Transportation be established to handle the matter. The shareholders' meeting of the Telephone Company is scheduled to be held at 4:00 PM today at the Royal Asiatic Society at 5 Museum Road to decide on the sale of the Telephone Company. The various reports heard yesterday are compiled as follows:

Letter and Telegram from the Commerce and Industry Reorganization Committee

The Commerce and Industry Reorganization Committee passed a resolution at its 56th Standing Committee meeting, notifying Chinese shareholders to unanimously oppose the sale of the Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company by the Concession Authorities and telegraphed a reply to the Ministry of Transportation. The telegram is recorded as follows:

(1) Reply to the Ministry of Transportation's Telegram, Nanjing Ministry of Transportation Junjian. Received your department's telegram of June 24th. The next day, a letter was also received from the city's telephone bureau, transcribing your department's confidential telegram. Under the reading, we have witnessed your department's eagerness to safeguard sovereignty, protect Chinese shares, and the interests of citizens. Therefore, it was submitted to the 56th Standing Committee meeting of the association on June 25th for discussion. It was unanimously agreed that the association has already scheduled a handover and is rushing to conclude all matters. Convening a meeting of all Chinese shareholders is already impossible. It was resolved to publish a notice to inform the Chinese shareholders of the company to unanimously oppose the sale to the International Company. The circumstances of the implementation of the telegram are respectfully reported. We ask your department to review and file the record for public convenience. Shanghai Special City Chamber of Commerce and Industry Reorganization Committee respectfully bows.

(2) Notice to Chinese Shareholders: Notice regarding the matter of receiving the Ministry of Transportation's telegram, stating that the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company's letter to shareholders and users was published in the Shen and Xin newspapers on the 21st (already seen in this newspaper on the 25th, omitted), etc. It was submitted to the 56th Standing Committee meeting on the 25th of this month for discussion. It was unanimously agreed that the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company and the Concession Authorities, disregarding the interests of Chinese shareholders, privately selling to foreigners, greatly hinders our country's public communication industry, which is different from ordinary buying and selling stores, and shows contempt for sovereignty. The Ministry of Transportation, based on our party's platform and planned policies, is actively preparing to take it back, which is to take care of the interests of the majority of Chinese shareholders and break the monopoly of the foreign directors of the company. All our Chinese shareholders should unite and strive to fight for the Ministry of Transportation to achieve the purpose of taking it back and saving our sovereignty, etc. A notice was issued to all Chinese shareholders to cooperate and insist on the resolution. It is sincerely hoped that all Chinese shareholders will unanimously oppose the sale to foreign merchants. This announcement is made with utmost anticipation.

Declaration of the Citizens' Association

The Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Special District Citizens' United Association held an emergency meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the issue of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company holding a special shareholders' meeting today to sell the special district's telephone business. More than 30 preparatory committee members attended, including Wu Liangsheng, Zhang Zilian, Wu Zhihao, Luo Qinghua, Jiang Xinzhao, Yu Mingxun, Yu Zhongxian, Hu Fengxiang, Yu Yangsheng, Cai Suizhi, Zhang Xianfang, Wang Pingnan, and Lu Qisheng. Zhang Yichen chaired the meeting. After the ceremony, Secretary Yue reported the original texts of the urgent telegram from the Ministry of Transportation and the official letter forwarded by the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, requesting serious opposition to the Shanghai Special District Telephone Company's sale of the Special District's telephone business to the International Company and assisting the Ministry of Transportation in formulating measures to take it back as soon as possible. The chairman reported the purpose of convening the emergency meeting today. Then, committee members such as Zhang Zilian, Lu Qisheng, Jiang Xinzhao, Hu Fengxiang, Yu Zhongxian, and Luo Qinghua successively stood up and proposed countermeasures. After discussion, it was concluded that the telephone is a public communication industry, which concerns national sovereignty and the welfare of citizens. It is difficult for the company to sell it to the International Company without authorization. They should represent all citizens and unanimously and seriously oppose it, and jointly work with public groups to implement the recovery measures. Finally, it was decided to take both symptomatic and fundamental measures:

(1) In the name of the association, publish a declaration in Chinese and foreign newspapers immediately, resolutely oppose it, and seriously warn Chinese shareholders and friendly shareholders of the company to express their opposition unanimously. Jiang Xinzhao and Luo Qinghua, two members, were publicly elected to draft the declaration on the spot.

(2) Send a letter to Chen Bingqian and other major Chinese shareholders of the company, seriously requesting them to pay attention and proceed consistently.

(3) The next plenary committee will continue to discuss specific measures and deliberate over the long term. After the discussion, other matters were discussed and adjourned. The attached declaration is as follows (omitted above):

Recently, I read the official announcement of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company that a special shareholders' meeting will be held today (27th) to prepare to accept the International Company's bid and implement the sale of the Special District's telephone service. The telephone is a public communication industry, which is completely different from ordinary buying and selling shops. How can it be sold without authorization? The Ministry of Transportation of the National Government, party headquarters at all levels, and various public groups have successively seriously opposed it and expressed remedial measures. In order to protect our national sovereignty and respect the party's platform, the association convened an emergency meeting on June 26th and unanimously passed a resolution to seriously oppose the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company's sale of the Special District's telephone business and advocate actively taking it back. It is hereby urgently announced that all compatriots of our country who hold shares of the company should respect the law and safeguard sovereignty. Please unanimously refrain from attending the company's special shareholders' meeting today and hope to quickly unite with all Chinese shareholders to actively oppose the company's proposal to show their support for national sovereignty and laws. In case they are blinded by the company and support the sale to foreign merchants, losing national rights and isolating themselves from the public, the association will only represent the citizens of the city to closely monitor and impose appropriate sanctions. Friendly people from all countries who hold shares in the company should also consider the friendly relations between our countries and not violate the feelings of the Chinese people, leading to various unfortunate events. In addition to jointly working with various groups to seek active countermeasures and submitting a request to the government for serious negotiations, the association first publishes this urgent notice in the newspaper due to the urgency of the situation. I hope everyone will pay attention to it. The Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Special City Special District Citizens' United Association.

Public Announcement of Chinese Users

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Chinese Users Association convened a meeting yesterday afternoon at the Bank Club and resolved the following two items:

(1) Send a letter to warn the authorities of the new company that is purchasing at a high price.

(2) Issue a declaration unanimously opposing it. The public announcement is recorded as follows:

To the Chinese Shareholders of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company:

Respectfully informing you that the business of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company has never been authorized by the Chinese government and is originally a violation of sovereignty. Now, while our government is preparing to take it back, the company turns a deaf ear and decides to sell it to the International Telegraph and Telephone Company, and the new company has the condition of obtaining a 40-year franchise. This kind of action not only despises our government but also disregards the interests of all our Chinese users. What was the attitude of the former Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company towards our Chinese users and shareholders? I think everyone can remember. This time, the new company actually spent a lot of money to purchase it. The intention is very obvious. May I ask where the interests of our Chinese users and shareholders will be guaranteed in the future? Therefore, we hereby unite and resolutely oppose it. We beg all Chinese shareholders to support national sovereignty and protect public interests. Do not attend the company's special shareholders' meeting on the 27th of this month. Any resolutions of the shareholders' meeting will not be recognized. This statement is hereby made. We hope you will take note of it. Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company Chinese Users Association, June 26th.

Director Zhuang's Remarks

Zhuang Zhihuan, director of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Transportation, told a reporter from Guowen News Agency yesterday that the Ministry of Transportation has repeatedly written to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs since September last year to recover the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company. The Municipal Council initially replied to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, saying that it had invited experts to investigate and prepare for improvement, so there was no result. During the recent second company bidding, it suddenly changed its policy and sold the original company. Therefore, the Ministry of Transportation actively opposed it in order to take care of national sovereignty and the interests of the people and advocated that Chinese people buy and operate it. The reasons are:

(1) The telecommunications industry should be state-owned in principle. Chinese companies can also be approved by the government. Now foreign merchants are buying the Chinese-foreign joint venture.

(2) The government and the people are actively recovering the concessions, and the grant of a 40-year patent is deliberately taking advantage.

(3) The interest rate required by the bidding company is too high, which will harm users.

(4) The Nanshi and Zhabei telephones in Shanghai are both operated by the Ministry of Transportation and are connected to the long-distance telephones of Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou, while the telephones in the special district are exclusively operated by foreign merchants, which will inevitably cause many inconveniences in communication.

(5) There are no foreign merchants operating telephones in other places. For example, the telephone in the Tianjin and Hankou concessions is also operated by the Ministry of Transportation. Now the Ministry of Transportation is very willing for Chinese merchants to operate it and does not advocate complete departmental operation. However, the Ministry has already prepared the necessary capital.

Tianjin Customs Affects Shipping 90

Almost All Chinese Merchants' Goods Have Stopped Shipping

The Inspector General of Customs, under the order of the National Government, announced that the Tianjin Customs will be considered to be under actual blockade. All import and export duties receivable by Tianjin Customs will be collected by the Jianghai Customs on its behalf, causing great difficulties for the shipping industries in Shanghai. The Chinese merchants' North China liners will formally suspend the Tianjin route. The various news obtained yesterday are recorded separately as follows:

Piece Goods Must Be Taxed

Piece goods merchants in Shanghai urgently need to ship a large quantity of goods to Tianjin. They telegraphed to Tianjin to inquire whether they can pick up the goods in Tianjin based on the red list after the import duty is collected by the Shanghai Customs on its behalf. Yesterday, Tianjin replied that [Quan piece goods and foreign cloth must be inspected and taxed by the customs before they can be unloaded, otherwise they will be detained]. Since yesterday, Chinese merchants' piece goods have completely stopped loading.

Taxable Goods Stop Shipping

Export goods are divided into two types: taxable and tax-free. For example, goods from the Yangtze River that are reported for transit to Tianjin must be taxed when they are transferred to Tianjin from Shanghai. If they have been reported for import in Shanghai, they do not need to be taxed when they arrive in Tianjin. Since the 24th, various North China merchants in Shanghai have agreed to completely stop loading taxable goods to Tianjin due to the loss of double taxation.

Foreign Ships Start to Come to Shanghai

After the blockade of Tianjin Customs, the first foreign merchant ships coming to Shanghai from Tianjin include the Japanese ship Chōhei Maru and the British ship Fushun. The ships have already imported. The foreign merchants' goods transported from Tianjin to Shanghai have already been implemented by not paying the standard tax (paid when loaded in Tianjin) and the half tax (paid when arriving in Shanghai) and immediately transferring them to the consulates of various countries for collection on their behalf. Now only foreign merchants' goods are still being loaded as usual between Shanghai and Tianjin.

Extreme Shortage of Goods Going to Tianjin

Since the 24th, the amount of goods going to Tianjin from Shanghai has been unprecedentedly low. Yesterday morning, a British ship exported a total of only 150 tons of goods to Yantai, Weihaiwei, and Tianjin, and the total freight was only 505 taels in gross amount. Another Chinese ship exported only 100 tons of goods to Yantai and Tianjin, and the freight earned was not enough to cover half the cost of coal. The Shanghai shipping industry considers it to be the first time since the Republic of China.

Chinese Ships Will All Suspend

Yesterday, Chinese shipping merchants in Shanghai were discussing that Chinese ships on the Tianjin route have never loaded foreign goods. Now that all the North China merchants have suspended export goods, the liners to Tianjin will be operating empty. Therefore, they decided to suspend the Tianjin route from the next voyage after the ships that have already left return to Shanghai.

Acting

Remarks by Director Tang Naikang of the Municipal Finance Bureau 95

Xu Fu, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau, resigned and was approved. The municipal government appointed Counselor Tang Naikang to act as the successor. The news was reported in yesterday's newspapers. Reporters from various newspapers visited Mr. Tang at the municipal government yesterday and asked him about the date of taking over and the financial policy to be implemented. According to Mr. Tang, I have very little experience in financial management and I am afraid that I will not be able to win the job. Since receiving the order, I have repeatedly resigned to Mayor Zhang, but I have not been invited to approve it. I reluctantly agreed to act as an agent temporarily until a suitable candidate is found. Moreover, Director Xu has organized the financial affairs of this city in an orderly manner and has achieved remarkable results. I uphold the principle of following Xiao's rules and Cao's legacy and take the four words of diligence, prudence, integrity, and cleanliness as the purpose of handling affairs. All financial revenues and expenditures are open so that citizens can understand the financial situation of the city and supervise it. Since the news of my acting as the Director of the Finance Bureau spread, many people have recommended talents. However, the Municipal Finance Bureau has been established for three years and the internal staff are all experienced. Moreover, I am only acting temporarily and it is not convenient to make many changes. Although there are virtuous people, there is no way to recruit them. I hope that all circles will forgive me for this point. As for the date of taking over, according to Mr. Tang, because Director Xu will soon hand over, it is planned to go to the Finance Bureau on July 1st to take over.

Tang Naikang

A Brief Biography of Director Tang

Mr. Tang is a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang. He is 42 years old, a member of the Kuomintang, a member of the Chinese Revolutionary Party, a graduate of Fudan University, and Zhejiang Higher School. After the restoration of the Republic of China, he successively served as the secretary of the Shanghai Military Governor's Office, the secretary of the Shanghai Army's Yuan Suppression Army Headquarters, and the head of the military supply section. After the Second Revolution, he founded the North Shanghai Public School in Shanghai and served as the principal, focusing on education. During the rise of the National Revolutionary Army, he successively served as the counselor of the General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, the magistrate of Deqing County, Zhejiang, the director of the Zhejiang Anti-Smoking Bureau, the director of the Finance Bureau of Nanjing Special City, a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Unilateral Regulations Compilation and Review Committee, a senior counselor of the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, a member of the Shanghai Special Municipal Construction Discussion Committee, a member of the Rice and Grain Evaluation Committee, a member of the Budget Committee, a member of the Committee for Raising Municipal Public Bonds, a member of the Preparatory Committee for the Implementation of the Municipal Organization Law, a member of the Preparatory Committee for the Municipal Annals Museum, a member of the Financial Reorganization Committee, and a member of the Municipal Public Bond Fund Management Committee.

Careful Discussion of the County Budget 97

Details of the Discussion on Reassessing Land Prices

The circumstances of the Shanghai County Government's discussion on reassessing land prices the other day were briefly reported in the newspapers. Now, the detailed investigation is recorded below. This time, the Jiangsu Provincial Government vigorously implements budget preparation. The Shanghai County Government and its subordinate bureaus and agencies are also striving to economize to ensure that the budget is established so that county administration can be carried out on the right track. For the past two weeks, it has been carefully planned. However, the county area is too small and the income is too short. After economizing, it is still not enough. At that time, the county government received a report from Huang Meixian, director of the county agricultural farm, stating that the farm's expenses were not covered and requested that agricultural improvement donations be collected. However, the previously assessed land price was too low. According to regulations, it cannot be increased by more than one percent of the land price. However, the average land price in Baoshan is more than 116 yuan per mu, and Songjiang is 110 yuan. Shanghai is adjacent, but the price per mu is only 100 yuan, which is too low. Therefore, he requested that it be reassessed. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Yan believed that it was undesirable to increase the burden on the people when the people's strength was difficult. However, the county budget could not be reduced and was indeed a fact. The county administration could not proceed, and the people who were directly harmed were still the people. Therefore, after careful consideration, he submitted this report to the last county administration meeting for public discussion. It was heard that the meeting decided to convene a meeting of various agencies and public groups the day before yesterday for discussion. It was heard that at the meeting that day, everyone recognized that the budget deficit was a real situation. If the budget is to be established, another method must be found to raise funds. However, some opinions believe that it would be better to find another method other than increasing taxes. Therefore, the result of the vote that day was that the votes in favor and against were the same at six votes. According to the common practice in the venue, the chairman should participate in the opinion to make a decision. However, Chairman Yan believed that this case was not a common case. Matters related to the burden on the people should be discussed in detail and the public opinion of local people should be respected. Therefore, he would rather retain this right and resubmit it to everyone attending the meeting for public discussion and request them to express specific opinions.

(1) If the expenses listed in the proposal are deemed to be reducible, please submit the items and numbers for discussion and decision, and the county government can do so as soon as possible.

(2) If it is deemed that it cannot be reduced any further, if there are other stable and legal methods of raising funds other than increasing taxes, please submit them for discussion. At that time, everyone attending the meeting had different opinions. It was generally believed that it was impossible to reduce the various expenses. Since it was getting late, the chairman decided to postpone the meeting until today (27th) at 1:00 PM for public consideration.

Content of the Proposal

The director of the County Agricultural Farm submitted a proposal to reassess land prices for public decision.

(1) Reasons for the Farm's Proposal

The farm's original expenses were subsidized by the province by 1,212 yuan per year, which was only one-third of the original budget. Now, the provincial subsidy has also been ordered by the department to stop allocating funds from July, resulting in no funds. If it is stopped immediately, the previous achievements will be abandoned. It is found that the average land price assessed this time is 100 yuan per mu. In fact, the total average land price in the county exceeds 100 yuan. Therefore, it is requested to reassess it and collect agricultural improvement donations as a precedent to maintain the farm's expenses.

(2) Opinions of the County Government

It is found that the county previously ordered the legal groups and farmer representatives to assess the land price on April 3rd in accordance with the order of the Finance Department and has not yet received instructions for approval. Therefore, the county's land price has not yet reached a certain period. Reassessing it is not impossible. According to the provincial gazettes, the average price of farmland in neighboring Baoshan County (Gazette No. 455) is 116 yuan per mu, and the average price of farmland in Songjiang (Gazette No. 457) is 110 yuan per mu. The price of farmland in this county should not be much lower than that of Baoshan and Songjiang. However, the average price assessed last time was only 100 yuan per mu, which is a big difference and should be discussed. In terms of taxation, it is better to keep the evaluation low for the sake of the current people's strength. If we consider the future land consolidation and collection for public use, then it is not good to be too low. It is necessary to consider both. It is found that the county has not many expenses for various undertakings. Now, the ones that can be slightly listed in the rushed budget for the 19th year (A. Party Affairs Expenses) have no funds at all and are temporarily transferred from provincial funds. It is difficult to transfer them again in the 19th year. According to regulations, this item requires a regular annual fee of 14,400 yuan, not including temporary expenses and mass organization expenses. (B. Autonomous Expenses) According to regulations, the district office expenses are 9,589 yuan short per year in addition to the original expenses. Even if the reduction is paid, at least 5,600 yuan must be raised. Although the township chiefs and village chiefs are volunteer positions, the office expenses are not named and it is difficult to handle all matters. This should also be planned for. (C. Farm Expenses) If there is no way to raise funds, then there is no choice but to stop it. (D. Charitable Relief Undertakings) There are many urgent matters to be handled but there is no way to handle them. It is also impossible to raise funds without lifting them. All of these major needs have been huge, and it is not easy to collect the funds without collecting them. If the land price is used as a percentage, such as the land price assessed according to the original evaluation, it will be difficult to levy it. The above-mentioned items cannot be resolved, and the budget for the 19th year will not be able to be compiled. This is related to the requirements of the budget. It is extremely important to reassess the land price and add a levy. Local undertakings cannot be stagnated, and increasing taxes will increase the burden on the people. It is difficult to take care of both. However, the expenses for undertakings that must be held must be planned in advance. Otherwise, it is still the burden of the people to dig wells when they are thirsty, or it will increase the invisible loss or take it harshly, which will only cause disputes. Rather than collecting scattered funds temporarily, which is also a burden on the people, it is better to collect taxes from farmland and turn the scattered into the whole. Therefore, for the farm's proposal and the needs of various undertakings, we still advocate adding a levy. Adding a levy must first determine the land price. This is the hope that the reassessment of the land price will be carefully explored and an appropriate solution can be obtained. This is the happiness of the future of local undertakings.

Baoshan County Government Budget Meeting 98

Baoshan County Chief Qiu Mingjiu convened a meeting of personnel from various agencies in the county government's assembly hall at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the 19th-year budget. County Chief Qiu, acting as chairman, reported on the approved levy of eight fen per mu of land. He then discussed the methods of allocation based on the actual revenue status of the 18th year, discounted by 88%.

(1) Yuan Guanlan and others requested that the grain storage fee be allocated from the eight fen per mu levy. It was unanimously decided to establish the case.

(2) It was unanimously decided to approve the proposal to allocate two fen from the grain storage fee, as originally requested.

(2) It was decided how to allocate funds for establishing a relief home, a smoking cessation center, and reorganizing the clinic. It was decided to allocate 1,000 yuan to the relief home for orphans and 1,000 yuan to the smoking cessation center attached to the medical clinic.

(3) It was decided to allocate 200 yuan to the county government gazette.

(4) It was decided to allocate 400 yuan to the party headquarters' temporary expenses.

(5) It was decided how to allocate funds for township and town offices and district projects. (1) 4,716 yuan was allocated to township and town offices (calculated at 3 yuan per month per office for 131 offices). (2) 3,000 yuan was allocated to district offices for project expenses (calculated at 50 yuan per month per district for five districts).

(6) It was decided to subsidize 1,000 yuan annually to address the insufficient funding of the registration bureau.

(7) The chairman proposed that, based on the actual collection situation, only 40% of the revenue could be collected in the first year. It was decided that the above-mentioned allocation amount was calculated based on the actual revenue status of the 18th year, discounted by 88%. In the future, if the full 88% could not be collected, it was decided that the shortfall should be proportionally allocated based on the actual revenue status and that the audit committee should conduct further estimation and review when preparing the 19th-year budget.

(8) It was decided to nominate the following members for the 19th-year budget audit committee: (1) Yuan Jietai, Director of the Finance Bureau; Wang Zhongqi, Director of the Property Department; Xue Ying, Section Chief of the Second Section of the County Government; Yin Shuqi, Director of the Registration Bureau; Lu Fengbo, District Chief of the Second District; Wang Cheng of the Education Bureau; and Zhang Jingshi of the County Party Headquarters. (2) If there were any changes to the budgets of various agencies, they should be submitted to the Finance Bureau before the 27th of this month. (3) It was decided to hold an audit meeting at 3:00 PM on the 29th of this month, convened by the Finance Bureau. All audit committee members should attend the county government meeting on the 30th to report.

The Case of Zhang Sixu's Detention 99

Foreign Minister Wang Prepares to Post Bail

The Shanghai Journalists Association representatives, Gu Angruo and Xia Boxun, visited Commander Xiong at the Longhua Headquarters yesterday afternoon to inquire about the truth of Zhang Sixu's detention. The reason for this could not be announced at the moment. He added that there was no danger in his detention, but he was being isolated from the outside world to stop his activities. Commander Xiong also instructed his secretary, Wang Zhiwen, to inform the military law office to give Zhang special treatment. Gu and Xia then went to the military law office to see Councilor Chen and Judge Advocate Dai. They both agreed that Zhang was a scholar and had moved Zhang to a special room with preferential treatment. Dai also allowed Gu and Xia, as well as Zhang's wife, to meet with Zhang. Minister Wang is also willing to guarantee Zhang Sixu's future actions in writing. Zhang's wife, as well as Powell, the editor of the "Millard's Review," and Li Cai, the president of the "National News Agency," are also making every effort to rescue him. Strict Investigation of Those Disrupting the Red Cross Assembly 101

Health Bureau Sends Letter to Chairman

Responsible for Reporting Within Three Days

During the previous general meeting of the Red Cross, some people organized thugs to disrupt the meeting place and destroy the general office. The National Government then telegraphed Shanghai Mayor Zhang and appointed Health Bureau Director Cha Fushe to investigate and respond. In accordance with the National Government's instructions, the matter should be reported by the chairman of the board of directors of the office. The Director of the Health Bureau then informed the chairman of the board, Wang Peiyuan, to comply. Yesterday, Wang Peiyuan replied to the Health Bureau, but the wording was vague and did not comply with the decree. Therefore, a letter was sent to Chairman Wang, urging him to strictly comply and respond to the original letter, stating that in the disturbance at the previous Red Cross general meeting election site, and the destruction of the Red Cross general office, there were traces of connection to the re-election. At that time, an effort was made to investigate the instigators and perpetrators in order to prosecute them according to law, but so far there has been no clue. We are still making every effort to investigate, and as soon as clear evidence is obtained, we will proceed with legal procedures. It is also heard that many representatives and members have submitted petitions to the National Government, begging them to forward requests for urgent investigation. Upon investigation, according to the facts and reasons stated in the previous order, the chairman of the board of directors of the general office should be responsible for reporting. Upon reviewing the reply letter from your chairman, the wording is ambiguous and there is no fact of taking responsibility for reporting. Moreover, the claim in the letter that dozens of people suddenly came with weapons at the time of the vote counting in the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, claiming that the ballots must be cancelled and a re-election held, Peiyuan replied that this was a matter for the general meeting and could not be answered at this moment, and the crowd roared for a long time before leaving. It is clear that your chairman had a close conversation with the thugs who were disrupting the meeting at that time, and it cannot be said that he did not know the instigators and helpers of the disruption and had no way to report them. It is also said that the disruption of the meeting place and the destruction of the general office are related to the re-election, but no one has been held responsible for reporting the disruption. The re-election committee had been working in your general office and had used the general office seal to issue notices. Moreover, your chairman and office staff Wei Ruifeng, Wu Yaosan, and Shen Jintao had served as members of the re-election committee until the Red Cross Standing Committee resolved to postpone the general meeting of members' representatives for three months before announcing their withdrawal from the re-election committee. It can be seen that your chairman and others were also closely connected with the side advocating for re-election. Since it is recognized that the disruption of the last election of the Red Cross and the destruction of the general office were all related to the re-election, then who instigated it? Who helped? There must be some knowledge. Why not take responsibility for reporting them in order to be sanctioned, but instead make ambiguous statements and say that the investigation has yielded no clues so far? It is the responsibility of your chairman to love the Red Cross, and he must be second to none in protecting the Red Cross from illegal infringement. He should break through feelings and have no scruples, and take responsibility for reporting in order to be able to present the facts separately and await legal sanctions and administrative punishments. It is still hoped that you will check the previous letter and respond truthfully within three days in order to comply with the decree and report this reply.

Proposals for the Committee to Promote Cholera Prevention 102

The Shanghai Municipal Cholera Prevention Propaganda Committee held its eighth regular meeting yesterday. After Chairman Ke Mizawa opened the meeting, each representative reported on the promotion and supervision of cholera prevention injections by their respective organizations last week.

(1) Yan Sen, representative of the Health Bureau, reported that a total of 166,217 people had received free cholera prevention injections from May 1st to June 24th, and that free injections were currently being promoted in various vegetable markets and on the water.

(2) The representative of the Public Security Bureau reported that orders had been repeatedly issued to all districts to earnestly take charge of supervising and urging people to receive injections.

(3) The representative of the Social Affairs Bureau reported that strict orders had been given to the responsible personnel of various factories and firms to supervise and urge people to receive injections.

(4) The representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters reported that notices had been distributed to all districts to inform all party members to cooperate in promoting and supervising people to receive injections.

The following matters were then discussed:

(1) The committee was asked to discuss the reply from the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration stating that advertising inside the carriages would be charged according to regulations, but that the cholera prevention illustrations could be charged at half price due to their public welfare nature. It was decided to reply to the railway administration that this matter was entirely of a public nature and that the display of posters encouraging cholera prevention was by no means comparable to commercial advertising. Moreover, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau also provided free cholera prevention injections, so it was requested that the posters be displayed free of charge to facilitate public awareness and emphasize epidemic prevention.

(2) A proposal was made to commend Yong'an Silk Factory, Weitong Yarn Factory, British American Tobacco Company, Shanghai Middle School, and other factories and schools for their excellent results in supervising and urging their workers or students to receive free cholera prevention injections. It was decided that the committee would send letters to each factory and school to express its appreciation for their concern for the health of their workers or students.

(3) A proposal was made to commend Cao, the head of the fourth precinct of the fifth district of the Public Security Bureau, for his extraordinary efforts in assisting with the supervision and urging of people to receive free cholera prevention injections. It was decided that the committee would send a letter to the Health Bureau, requesting that it, at the end of this round of preventive injections, refer to the regulations for rewarding and punishing the Public Security Bureau's various districts and branches for assisting with health administration and send a letter to the Public Security Bureau to reward them.

(4) A proposal was made to adjust the date of the committee's regular meetings. It was decided that the committee would meet once every two weeks on Wednesday afternoon at 2:00 PM during the second week. If there were any urgent matters, the Health Bureau representative would issue a notice to convene an extraordinary meeting.

Shipping News 104

Wuhu Invited All Circles to Visit Yesterday

Tonghua Escaped Danger: The Merchant Shipping Bureau's Haizhou liner Tonghua ran aground at Dapu. After ten days, the bureau sent a machine to Dapu to dig out the sand and mud from the third hold of the Tonghua. The ship was successfully towed out during high tide on the 25th. Yesterday, the ship telegraphed that it had arrived in Haizhou and was unloading cargo. The hull was undamaged, and the cargo was safe. It is expected to return to Shanghai tomorrow.

Wuhu to Start Service: The Taikoo Company's newly built Shanghai-Xuancheng liner Wuhu is fast and has excellent passenger accommodations. Since arriving in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the 24th, the ship docked at the company's wharf on the Bund outside the French Concession yesterday afternoon. The ship's grand dining room is located on the upper deck, and the officer and steerage cabins are beautifully arranged on the second deck. It is truly the best on the Shanghai-Yixing route. Shanghai to Xuancheng takes eight days. A seat in the grand dining room costs eighty yuan, an officer's cabin costs fifty yuan, and a steerage cabin costs only fourteen yuan and ten cents. The maiden voyage will start this morning. Yesterday, all circles were invited to visit. Those who attended included Yu Qiaqing, Sun Meitang, Yuan Ludeng, Yue Zhenbao, Chen Fenggang of the Sichuan gang, Liu Bingyi, Tang Bomou, managers of various customs brokers, and reporters from various newspapers, totaling several hundred people. Many British and Japanese people also attended. Chen Xuejia, the company's Chinese manager, Yang Shaonan, the head of the navigation department, and staff members Chen Kangqi and Dong Zhichu warmly welcomed the visitors. The ship is made entirely of steel, has a deadweight of 1,800 tons, and is very fast, traveling 14 nautical miles per hour. Both passengers and cargo are fully booked for the initial voyage.

Rice Price Rises to Twenty-Four Yuan 105

The Guowen News Agency reports that the price of rice has been rising daily due to the scarcity of goods arriving from various places. The actual black market price of first-class white rice has risen to twenty-four yuan per dan. Although the Social Affairs Bureau has issued restrictions, it is impossible to suppress the price. The reason for this is that the amount of rice arriving from the rice-producing areas is decreasing due to various factors such as weather and human affairs, resulting in a shortage of supply and a demand that cannot be met even with high prices. Moreover, the import prices of foreign rice such as Laimai and Ximai have also risen to around eighteen yuan. It is impossible to control the price of rice. There is a risk of a rice shortage forming in a month or two.

Yesterday's News on the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Strike 106

The French Concession water and electricity workers' strike is gradually expanding and is difficult to resolve. At 3:00 PM yesterday, the entire union held its fourth general meeting of all members at the Public Stadium. The Municipal Party Headquarters still sent Xu Yefu to attend and provide guidance. The Second District Headquarters of the Public Security Bureau sent police to maintain order. Chairman Xu Amei reported that the factory continued to stubbornly hire White Russians to work and that the company had still made no offers.

As reported yesterday, trams in the British and French Concessions cannot directly reach each other. However, the French Concession only blocked trolleybuses routes 14, 17, and 18 and not completely. Starting yesterday, the five tram routes connecting the British and French Concessions also remained closed.

Since the workers' strike began, the factory has suffered a lot of damage to its machinery. Although White Russians have been hired to repair it, it is still insufficient. It is reported that the factory once consulted the British Concession Tram Company, intending to ask the British factory workers to come to the French factory for repairs. The British factory foreman then sought the opinion of the British factory union, but they did not give their permission. Therefore, at around 10:00 AM yesterday, the British factory union sent two representatives to the French factory union to declare their refusal to help the French factory in order to express their spirit of mutual assistance. All the workers in the French factory union were very grateful upon hearing this.
