Local News from Suzhou

Huang Huiru Appears 108

Is It True or False?

Doubt Upon Doubt

Huang Huiru, of the Huang-Lu case, has been silent for a long time. Recently, it was rumored in Suzhou that Huang Huiru had not died and was hiding in Suzhou. Although the reporter found the rumor incredible, the details were strange. Therefore, yesterday (26th), the reporter went to the residence of Huang Zhu at No. 23 Xizhi Lane, Daoqian Street, Xumen in Suzhou to find out the truth. However, the door was closed, and there was no way to enter. So the reporter asked the nearby neighbors if they had seen Huang Huiru. According to a neighbor, there was indeed a young lady in the Huang residence who looked similar to the Huang Huiru described in previous reports, only slightly thinner. Recently, the young lady has been sick from time to time and has been treated with medicine, but has now recovered. Every day at 5 or 6 pm, she opens the door and stands. If a neighbor looks at her, she turns around and goes inside. Although the reporter cannot be sure that it is Huang Huiru, there must be a reason for the rumor, so it is recorded here for verification.

Monk Castrates Himself 109

Disgusted by Other Monks' Unclean Roots

To Declare His Innocence

Yu Xinfa, a 29-year-old from Hubei, was forced into a temple as a monk when he was young due to the death of his parents and the villainy of others. Last year, he came to Shanghai from his hometown and joined the Pushengtang at 36 Hujia Muqiao. He usually recites scriptures, worships Buddha, and strictly abides by the rules, so he is quite favored by the abbot. However, there are still several monks in the hall who cannot abide by the rules because their six roots are not clean, and they regard prostitution and whoring as commonplace. Yu was very disapproving and tried to persuade them, but his words were ignored. Yesterday afternoon, Yu once again encouraged his colleagues, which was met with ridicule from the monks, who slandered him as a hypocrite. Yu was displeased when he heard this and made a vow in public. To declare his innocence, he grabbed a kitchen knife, pulled down his trousers, and cut off his testicles, causing profuse bleeding. The monks quickly grabbed the knife and reported to the Fifth District Third Precinct, ordering the police to come and hire a car to take him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, Yu's life is still in danger.

Two Bandits in Kidnapping Case

Still Sentenced to Death After Retrial 110

Ma Jiyuan, a Henan native who previously served as a patrolman, and Liu Fuxing, a Suzhou native, repeatedly committed kidnappings of Chen Xiaofu, Xu Fusun, Ye Daming, and others in the past two years. They were arrested by the Jing'an Temple patrol and handed over to the former Provisional Court for questioning. They were sentenced to death and submitted to the higher authorities for review. Recently, an order was received to send the case back for retrial due to some doubts in the case. The Special District Local Court judge Sun Yuan reissued summonses for witnesses and researched the case of Ma and Liu. Yesterday morning, the verdict was announced: Ma Jiyuan and Liu Fuxing should be sentenced to death for their kidnapping and extortion, and deprived of their public rights indefinitely. After the sentencing, the patrolmen took them back to the Western Prison to await execution after confirmation.

Ge's Banxia Store

Inheritance Case Awaiting Sentencing 111

Yesterday's Debate Concluded

Ge Fengyuan's lawyer, Ge Fengyuan, hired Wu Zhiping and Ye Fukang as lawyers in the local court to sue his great-grandmother Ge Xu and his cousin Ge Jimei for infringement. He asked for the case to be filed and judged, stating that the plaintiff's uncle Yanting Gong was the first defendant. Ge Xu's eldest son, Min Ba, died without children, only a married daughter, Ge Jimei, the second defendant. With the approval of the plaintiff, the first defendant signed a succession agreement in May of the 18th year, choosing the plaintiff as Yanting Gong's heir. All property, except the house at No. 137 Lindun Road in Suzhou, was gifted to the second defendant. The remaining residential building at No. 507 Lindun Road in Suzhou, as well as the Ge Lao Er Fang Yu Qing Tang Banxia store in Shanghai, Suzhou, and Ningbo, will forever be jointly owned by the plaintiff and his cousin Fenghua. The succession was determined, and lawyer Lu Hongyi arrived at the scene to prove the matter and requested the Wu County Local Court to file and approve the agreement and publish a notice to the family. Unexpectedly, the second defendant was still not satisfied and dared to ask the first defendant to privately write a document transferring the already analyzed and determined Shanghai Banxia branch store to the second defendant, and asked the court to approve the record. Therefore, the plaintiff requested to revoke the document and take back the management himself, demanding that the transfer document be declared invalid and order the Shanghai Ge Lao Er Fang Banxia store to be returned to the plaintiff for self-management.

The Defendants' Response: The defendants, Ge Xu and Ge Jimei, hired Zhao Chuanding and Lu Congzu as lawyers to submit their responses. Jimei's defense briefly stated that the plaintiff claimed that the Shanghai Ge Lao Er Fang Yu Qing Tang Banxia Pharmacy had been recorded in the succession agreement as jointly owned by the plaintiff and his cousin Fenghua. Regardless of whether the succession agreement is recognized by the defendant's grandmother, the agreement is indeed suspicious in practice. For example, the Nanjing Ge Lao Er Fang Banxia store was established by the defendant after the death of the defendant's father, which the grandmother knew and would never have recorded it. Furthermore, there are still Yanting Gong's estates that are not recorded in the succession agreement. If the property division method in the succession agreement was the grandmother's intention, why would there be omissions? Also, the house at No. 137 Lindun Road in Suzhou was sold by the grandmother to the Zhang family in the same area as early as 1927. How could the grandmother not know this and still record it in the succession agreement? Furthermore, the advertisement in the Shanghai News and Suzhou Xiaobao on June 6, 1929, issued by lawyer Lu Hongyi on behalf of Ge Xu and Fengyuan, only stated that Fengyuan was chosen as Yanting Gong's heir to inherit the family lineage, and did not mention a single word about the estate division. Moreover, the defendant is Yanting Gong's only biological daughter, so why was she not notified in advance? In summary, it can be proved that the records in the succession agreement were not from the grandmother's own intention. Therefore, the grandmother's separate writing to return the management rights of the Shanghai pharmacy, which had already been inherited and obtained, to the defendant is fundamentally legal and does not involve the slightest infringement. As for the Shanghai Banxia store, Yanting Gong had said before his death that he would give it to the defendant to inherit, and when Yanting Gong was buried in 1919, because there were no biological children or heirs, the entire family agreed that the defendant would serve as the filial child and inherit the property. The children and grandchildren of the same family are all beyond the fifth degree of mourning (the defendant's father's branch has been transmitted alone for nine generations), and according to the law, there is no provision that disallows a biological daughter from inheriting the property. When the National Army arrived in Jiangsu in 1927, the defendant's inheritance of Yanting Gong's property as an unmarried daughter became even more fixed. The plaintiff's claim began in May 1929, at which time the property of the Shanghai Ge Lao Er Fang Yu Qing Tang Banxia store had already been obtained by the defendant through inheritance. If the so-called succession agreement did stipulate the division method of the Banxia store, the most unauthorized disposition would be invalid under the law and could not allow the plaintiff to interfere. In summary, the inheritance of the family lineage and the inheritance of property are two separate matters, and the inheritance of property by a woman and the inheritance by an heir are not mutually exclusive. Now, the plaintiff's claim to the estate, which had already been inherited and obtained by others, under the status of an heir who has not yet been determined, is extremely absurd and should be dismissed.

Yesterday, the case continued to be heard. Zeng Feng opened the court to hear the case, but it was not concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo Shouyi specially opened the Second Court to continue the hearing. Both parties, along with their lawyers, were present in court. The plaintiff Ge Fengyuan stated that his great-grandmother Ge Xu was blind, so the signature on the succession was done by Xu Xiaofeng. The judge asked how old Fenghua was, and the reply was seven years old, and it was Wang Zhimei who helped him sign. The judge asked if Jimei was present at the signing, and the reply was no. The judge asked why not, and the reply was because the house had already been given to her, so she was not present. The judge questioned Ge Jimei, who claimed that the Nanjing store was established with her investment. The judge asked Ge Xu if Xu Xiaofeng helped her sign, and the reply was yes, but they were holding my hand. The judge asked why she did not publish a statement, and the reply was that she only knew about the succession agreement and nothing else. The judge asked Ge Fengyuan if anyone had mediated outside, and the reply was no. The judge then announced the start of the debate, with the lawyers of both parties debating for a long time. The judge announced the conclusion of the debate and adjourned to await sentencing.

China Youth

Farewell Banquet for the Asia Walking Tour Group 112

The Chinese Youth Asia Walking Tour Group, which is scheduled to depart on the 28th of this month, was given a grand farewell banquet yesterday noon at Jue Yuan, No. 19 Hart Road, by prominent figures from all walks of life in Shanghai. In addition to the eight members of the group, including the group leader Li Mengsheng, Feng Binghun, Hu Sujuan, Cui Xiaoqiong, Huang Yue, Qiu Langming, Chen Wu, and Wang Xiahun, the attendees included Ye Gongchuo, Master Taixu, Ge Gongzhen, Liao Maoru, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Binhe, Shao Yizhi, Chen Bofan, Lin Liehfu, Zheng Zhizhong, Guo Xiqi, and Shao Woyun. First, Ye Gongchuo gave a lengthy lecture, the gist of which was that walking is the greatest of actions, but only by setting a goal and being down-to-earth can one achieve final success. After speaking, he personally inscribed the words "Courageous and Vigorous Progress" for the group. Next, the newspaper reporters took photos, and then everyone took their seats. The first speaker was Ge Gongzhen, who encouraged the group to proceed steadily, listen more and talk less, and keep records at all times and in all places. Next, Lin Liehfu gave a speech, the gist of which was that walking is the best way out for Chinese youth. Japanese people travel extensively within China every year, while Chinese people are living in a drunken stupor. We should catch up quickly. Finally, Huang Jingwan delivered a farewell speech, encouraging the group to strive forward, explore through walking, seek knowledge in practice, promote culture, connect feelings, urgently seek the liberation of weak nations, and advocate the organization of a Nanyang federation. Next, the leader of the group gave a thank-you speech, the gist of which was to state that the group's goal is to observe the lives of various ethnic groups at all times and in all places, with the whole world as one university, to keep walking tirelessly, and to have absolutely no political background, hoping to give Chinese youth a profound impression. After the banquet, Master Taixu also inscribed a text as a farewell gift. Newspaper reporters took many photos and presented the group with various books, magazines, and printed materials. The gathering ended happily at 4 p.m. The group is scheduled to gather at the North Station at 10 a.m. tomorrow to depart.

Wenzhou Sailing Ship Capsizes 113

The ship and cargo were completely lost.

The crew was rescued by the Guangji.

The merchant ship Guangji of the China Merchants Bureau rescued three sailors from a capsized sailing ship in the waters off Wenzhou while sailing from Shanghai. The news is reported as follows:

The Guangji found a sailing ship in distress off Daiman Mountain. On the 21st, the Guangji sailed from Wenzhou to Shanghai and discovered a capsized sailing ship in the waters off Daiman Mountain. At that time, it had not completely sunk. Tang Hesheng, the captain of the Guangji, ordered the ship to approach the sunken ship and heard calls for help from the sea. Using binoculars, he saw three people in the water near the sailing ship. Tang ordered the ship to stop and immediately dispatched First Officer Li Mingao and Second Officer Shen Cai to lower a boat and risk approaching the sailing ship. They rescued the three people in distress and brought them aboard.

The sailors recounted their ordeal. The three rescued people, named Wu Xianji, Wu Maoqing, and Wu Xiaomao, were said to be the owners of the sailing ship. After being brought aboard the Guangji, Tang provided them with clothing and food and inquired about their ordeal. They said that they were sailing to Zhou when they encountered a strong wind in the waters off Daiman Mountain at 2 p.m. on the 21st. The ship capsized, and all the cargo and belongings were lost. After falling into the sea, no ships passed by, and they thought they had no chance of survival until they were rescued. The three were brought to Shanghai by the Guangji.

The distressed passengers were sent back to Wenzhou. The three rescued people were immediately taken in on board. Since they had no relatives or friends in Shanghai, Tang Hesheng, the captain of the Guangji, reported the matter to the headquarters, which ordered the ship to return them to Wenzhou. Yesterday, Wu Xianji and the others left Shanghai on the Guangji. It is said that the wrecked sailing ship broke up and sank to the bottom of the sea within three hours. Zhao Tieqiao has ordered that Tang Hesheng and the crew of the Guangji be commended for respecting the maritime distress convention and rescuing the people who fell into the sea.

Secretary of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce

Marshall Did Not Intend to Commit Suicide 114

No financial or family difficulties.

It was an accidental discharge while cleaning a gun.

Marshall, the secretary of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, died the other day as a result of an accidental discharge of a gun while cleaning it. According to a report in Bazhi yesterday, Mr. Marshall wrote two letters that afternoon, one to his wife. The British Consulate has requested the post office to return them for examination. When the police heard the news, they immediately sent officers to the General Chamber of Commerce to investigate. According to Hua De, the vice-secretary of the Chamber of Commerce, he had known Mr. Marshall for fifteen years and had never heard of him having any financial or family problems. He did not think that he had intended to commit suicide. After the examination, the body was moved to the International Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road for funeral arrangements. Mr. Marshall had served the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for nearly twenty years and left behind a wife and two daughters, all of whom are in Vancouver, as well as the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company.

Laying Water Pipes on Jiangwan Road 115

The Public Works Bureau pays attention to traffic.

The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company needs a large amount of water in the area west of the Songhu Railway on Jiangwan Road. It plans to lay six-inch water pipes on Jiangwan Road from the front of the Sichuan Merchants Association to the Faculty of Law to expand the water supply. The Municipal Public Works Bureau reported that the road is an important traffic artery from Zhabei to Jiangwan and is also the route of the first public bus line for Chinese merchants. Therefore, it ordered the company to pay attention to three matters: (1) When digging the road, space should be left for public buses or freight cars to pass through. (2) The excavated soil and water pipes should be piled up in a place that does not obstruct the passage of vehicles. (3) The edges of the excavated road trench must be supported with plank piles and cross braces to prevent collapse due to the vibration of passing vehicles. If vehicles are damaged as a result, the company shall be responsible. Subsequently, the company re-submitted and was approved by the Public Works Bureau to mark the excavation warning signs with the words "[Vehicles must not exceed ten miles per hour]" to avoid danger.

National Photography Exhibition Opens Today 116

No admission tickets required.

The long-awaited National Photography Exhibition, initiated by the Chinese Photographic Society, will open at 9 a.m. this morning on the eighth floor of the China United Assurance Company, opposite the racecourse on Jing'an Temple Road. The exhibition hall has been specially arranged by the Society, with exceptionally sufficient light. Luxurious chairs are available opposite the photos for detailed viewing. From the window, one can see most of Shanghai. Visitors can take the elevator directly to the eighth floor. There are 210 photographic works on display, all of which are the products of photographic comrades from all over the country. Prizes awarded by various circles are also displayed in the hall. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Wusong Opens a Fair Price Rice Bureau 117

The Wusong Municipal Committee Office, in view of the recent high price of rice, which has reached its extreme, has been granted by the Special Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's Fair Price Rice Committee 200 shi of fair price rice (i.e., Saigon rice). It arrived in Wusong yesterday afternoon and is priced at 15 yuan per shi. The fair price rice will be sold starting from the 28th of this month, from 8 a.m. to 12 p.m. and from 2 p.m. to 4 p.m. daily. Large households will be given one sheng, and small households will be given half a sheng. The fair price rice distribution point is located at the Wusong Jisheng Sub-Association Storage Office on Shihe Road. The staff will be dispatched jointly by the Municipal Committee Office and the Rice and Grain Trade Association. The method is that the local baojia will first investigate the poor households and issue fair price rice purchase certificates in order to benefit the poor and relieve the needy.

The 2nd Battalion of the 27th Regiment of the 13th Brigade of the 5th Division of the Army stationed in Shanghai returned to Shanghai after suppressing bandits in Qidong. They arrived in Song on the Hongxing ship yesterday morning and docked at the grain and rice wharf to disembark. They then took a train to Shanghai to return to their defensive positions.

Tailor

Dies of Sudden Illness During Epidemic 119

Huang A'san, a tailor from Dapu, Guangdong, aged 48, went to the Xin Xin Dafang Inn at No. 18 Baoyu Lane, French Concession, alone at 8 p.m. the night before and asked to borrow a room, paying a room fee of 7 jiao. He then went out and returned to the inn at 2 a.m. late at night with a young woman, Huang Zhang, and her son, Huang Yongsheng, to sleep. Unexpectedly, at 5 a.m. the next morning, Zhang suddenly fell ill with diarrhea and died shortly thereafter. The tea room attendant informed the inn owner, Xu Debiao, who reported it to the Da Zi Ming Zhong police station. The police chief ruled that she had died of illness and instructed the relatives to collect the body themselves. Huang then tried to buy a coffin and hastily made arrangements for burial. Since there was no place to store the coffin, he requested the assistance of the Tongren Fuyuan Hall to bury it in a charitable cemetery for future retrieval. The police station, considering that an epidemic had suddenly occurred in the inn and that the summer weather was hot, feared that it would spread and endanger the lives of the public and passengers. Therefore, they notified the Health Department to send a Western doctor to inspect the inn and spray disinfectant in each room to kill the disease and protect hygiene.

Please pursue 20,000 yuan in alimony

The statement of claim roughly stated that the defendant seduced her into engagement and abandoned her after the fact, requesting a judgment to pay alimony. First, the plaintiff's eldest daughter, Erbao, was waiting to be married and had not been promised to anyone. In July of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the defendant sent his factory partner, Zhang A'zhao, to act as a matchmaker and formally engaged her to the defendant, stating that he had no wife. The plaintiff repeatedly refused because the defendant's family owned hundreds of thousands of gold, a wealth that was not a good match. However, on the 19th of a certain month in the 18th year, the defendant took advantage of her being unprepared to seduce Erbao and commit adultery, not allowing her to go home. On November 19, it was discovered that she was renting a house at No. 240 Longmen Road. The plaintiff heard about it and went to bring her to the police station, but the defendant kowtowed and begged for forgiveness, asking her not to publicize it, and promised to prepare a gift and marry her within a month. However, it was repeatedly postponed without any sincerity. Later, it was discovered that the defendant already had a wife. The previous marriage proposal, falsely claiming that he was unmarried, was clearly a seduction. If he had mistakenly believed that there was a marital relationship, it would have constituted a criminal offense. Unexpectedly, the defendant went even further and suddenly sent a letter through representative lawyer Gu Changyuan this month, instructing the plaintiff to go to the law firm to negotiate, otherwise he would file a lawsuit. The defendant, relying on his wealth, intended to use his power to bully people and force her to break the engagement, abandoning her after the fact, which was clear. A woman's chastity is important, and now she has been abandoned halfway. According to one-twentieth of the defendant's property, the following requests are made: (1) Order the defendant to pay the plaintiff Erbao 10,000 yuan in alimony. (2) The plaintiff Erbao's daily life cannot be maintained, and she requests that the defendant's proposal be submitted for bail. (3) The defendant bears the court fees, etc. After Judge Gong Jun approved the application, the defendant was summoned yesterday but did not appear. The judge instructed the case to be adjourned for seven days and the defendant summoned again for questioning based on the plaintiff's lawyer's statement of the case.

Xiaoribao Huang Guangyi is Innocent 131

Reversal of the Case of "Shè Liè Jì"

Xiaoribao was previously sued by the police station for publishing an article "Shè Liè Jì" because the words were obscene and considered harmful to public morals. The court issued a ticket to summon Huang Guangyi, the publisher of the newspaper, and sentenced him to a fine of 200 yuan. However, Gangbao was also accused of publishing "Shè Liè Jì" and was only fined 50 yuan. Therefore, Gangbao immediately paid the fine, while Huang Guangyi was unconvinced and hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to appeal to the local court of the same level. The reason was that there were seven shareholders of Xiaoribao, and Huang Guangyi only accounted for one-seventh of the shares. There were five editors, and the chief editor was You Bankuang. In terms of status and responsibility, Huang should not be solely responsible. He requested a reversal and dismissal of the original judgment, etc. The case was sent to Zhou Han, the president of the local court, for a hearing. After Chen further debated based on legal principles, Zhou publicly ruled yesterday afternoon to dismiss the original judgment and declare Huang Guangyi innocent. You Bankuang, who should be held responsible, has also been summoned by the primary criminal court of the same court for questioning and sentenced to a fine of 100 yuan as a warning.

Business Integration Association

Guaranteeing Residential Rights of Members 136

A Letter from the Trade Association to the Xiao Company

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in order to protect the residential rights of its members in the trade, yesterday sent a letter to the Xiao Company, which manages rental properties. The letter stated: "Regarding the matter of the Trade Association's letter stating that its members, Shi Rui Ji and Xin Xie Shun, received a letter from the North Shanghai Tax Collection Office, which was forwarded by the Xiao Fang branch of Baoshan Road, saying that the houses of these two firms have been re-rented to the Municipal Bank and should be vacated immediately with appropriate moving expenses provided, otherwise, barriers will be erected on the 15th of this month. These two firms have been doing business here since the early years of the Republic, and their customers are familiar with them. Relocation would make it difficult for them to maintain their business. Furthermore, after suffering from looting by Fengtian troops, their vitality has not recovered. Afterwards, the landlord rebuilt the premises, and the rent and fees paid for each building have reached more than two hundred yuan, plus additional renovations. We request that you find a way to help them so that they can maintain their business. The Association has dispatched personnel to negotiate with the Municipal Bank. According to the Vice-Manager of the Bank, Mr. Chen Zhangwen, the bank is willing to provide more relocation expenses if the stores are willing to move, but will not force them to move. Furthermore, a letter from the North Shanghai Tax Collection Office of the Bureau of Finance replied that this case was only negotiated with the Xiao Company and did not involve direct contact with merchants, nor was it enforced by the Public Security Bureau. How can it be called forced lease? The Association believes that since the Municipal Bank does not intend to force the stores to move and does not want to rent them, and the North Shanghai Tax Collection Office denies any forced lease, the key to resolving this matter lies entirely with your rental office. These two stores have been renting and doing business here for nearly twenty years, and their customers are familiar with them. Relocation would inevitably make it difficult to maintain their business. These stores are small-scale businesses and their situation is extremely pitiful. From the standpoint of humanitarianism and out of consideration for the many years of good relations in renting the entire property, it is necessary to give this due consideration. Moreover, putting aside sentiment and reason, the law states that since the tenants have not defaulted on their rent, and the landlord is not taking back the property for their own use, according to recent court decisions in this city, if the tenants do not voluntarily agree to move, the landlord cannot force them to move. Your rental office is presumably aware of this point, and should not stubbornly ignore it. Therefore, we have prepared this letter to request that you allow these two stores to continue renting the premises so that they can conduct their business in peace. This is our sincere hope. To the Xiao Company Rental Office."

On the Causes of the Fall in Silver Prices 137

Translated by the World News Agency from the London Economic Times: The world's silver production last year totaled 25,650,000 ounces, slightly less than Mexico's production in 1928. Mexico accounted for 42 percent of this total, and the United States accounted for 24 percent. In the previous decade, the world's silver production increased by about 48 percent. The increase in the United States was limited. Other major silver-producing countries are Canada, Peru, and Australia. Seventy-five percent of the world's silver production is used for coinage, and more than twenty percent is used for arts and crafts. Last year, India and China absorbed 70 percent of the world's silver production. China accounted for 13,700,000 ounces and India accounted for 8,200,000 ounces. One of the main reasons for the current fall in silver prices is that some countries have stopped minting silver coins, causing the demand for silver to shrink sharply. The Indian government has adopted the gold standard and is now selling its silver reserves. As for the Kemmerer Commission's proposals in China to gradually adopt the gold standard to consolidate the currency system, it is feared that this will soon be implemented, and the use of silver will also be drastically reduced. Another reason is the reduction in the fineness of silver coins. In 1928 alone, the fineness of silver coins reduced by England, France, and Belgium reached a huge 38 million ounces. The fall in silver prices has most affected silver producers. For example, the Burma Silver Mining Company mined 7,376,841 ounces of silver in the year ending June 30 last year. The relationship between income and expenses is very significant, and the stock values of various silver mining companies will also inevitably fall. As for trade between Manchester and China, it is still based on silver. After the fall in silver prices, transactions have sharply decreased, causing great difficulties.

Declaration of the Zhufeng Trade Union Requesting Assistance 138

Regarding the Temporary Closure of the Factory

The Zhufeng Enamel Factory Trade Union's declaration to all sectors requesting assistance regarding the factory's temporary closure states: "To all newspaper offices, fellow countrymen, and fellow workers in the city, please be advised that since the signing of the agreement with the capital last year, there has been no practical improvement in the conditions. However, we always hoped that the factory would be understanding, so we endured and worked hard. Unexpectedly, the factory not only failed to understand the workers but also intensified its oppression. Recently, because we requested rice subsidies, the factory unconditionally announced a temporary closure, leaving 500 fellow workers with no means of livelihood. The Labor Dispute Resolution Law is something that all capitalists must abide by, even imperialist capitalists must absolutely abide by it when setting up factories in our Chinese territory. The capitalists of our Zhufeng Factory have stubbornly and openly violated this. Since the Hong case occurred, the factory has dismissed seven workers without notifying the trade union or submitting it to the Social Bureau [because Article 3 of our agreement states that the company shall not dismiss workers without cause, and if they are dismissed for cause, the reasons shall be announced and the trade union notified]. Therefore, based on the facts at the time and the court's evidence [because the court denied that the seven were responsible for injuring Hong], we protested and requested mediation. While mediation was in progress, the factory unconditionally announced a temporary closure as a means of intimidation. Article 35 of Chapter 4 of the Labor Dispute Resolution Law states that employers or laborers may not commence a strike or closure during the mediation or arbitration period. This proves the factory's violation of regulations and also proves that the factory is using the Hong case as a pretext to deprive workers of their livelihood. The trend of gold being expensive and silver being cheap is intensifying day by day, and the price of rice has also increased to 24 yuan. The high cost of goods has also increased significantly. Workers' lives are becoming increasingly difficult under the pressure of the environment, especially the workers in the enamel industry (average of 15 yuan per month per person), it is even more difficult to sustain themselves. In order to preserve our families' lives, we workers can only ask the capitalists who employ us for subsidies. Moreover, our request is very modest (a subsidy of 5 yuan per person when the price of rice is above 18 yuan, a subsidy of 3 yuan per person when the price of rice is below 18 yuan, and the subsidy is cancelled when the price of rice is 14 yuan). The factory has ample room to accommodate this. Now the factory not only refuses to accept this but also uses an unconditional temporary closure to cut off the workers' livelihood. This proves the ironclad evidence of the Zhufeng Factory's oppression of workers. Dear fellow countrymen, what possibility of liberation is there for us workers of the Zhufeng Factory under this kind of threatening oppression? How can we find a life? The slogan of justice overcoming power will never be extinguished or changed under the blue and white flag. However, we, with our weak abilities, are especially afraid that our strength will be insufficient. We hope that all party and government organs, fellow countrymen from all walks of life, and fellow workers in Shanghai will come to help us oppressed workers emerge from the water and fire and ascend to a comfortable seat. Our association respectfully leads all 500 workers in the factory to offer incense and prayers, and earnestly presents these words in the hope of public judgment. Respectfully presented by the Zhufeng Enamel Factory Trade Union of the Shanghai Special Municipality, leading all 500 workers."

Hua Yang Charity Association

Xinghua Relief Report 139

This year, northern Jiangsu is experiencing a spring famine, with Xinghua being the most severely affected area. Local Chinese and Western individuals organized a Xinghua Hua Yang Charity Relief sub-association. The Shanghai Hua Yang Charity Relief Association allocated funds for relief efforts. The relief effort has now concluded, and the sub-association has reported on the progress of the relief efforts, which are transcribed as follows: "The sub-association has received a total of 10,050 yuan in relief funds from the association, 3,000 yuan in relief funds from the Xinghua relief sub-association, and 110.02 yuan from other sources, for a total of 13,160.02 yuan in relief funds. The temporary relief tickets from the Jiangsu Provisional Charity Relief Association were borrowed and stamped with the sub-association's seal. These tickets were sent to the Fifth District to issue them. The district has a total of 14 map regions, 366 villages, and 3,420 households. The tickets were issued based on the severity of the disaster and the number of family members, divided into six grades represented by the six characters 'An Ding Jing An Lv De', representing 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 yuan. The tickets were issued at the Grandma Temple in Anfeng Town on May 30 of this year, with the Xinghua County Magistrate present to supervise. A total of 3,420 relief tickets were issued, totaling 12,298 yuan. A subsidy of 300 yuan was provided to the Anfeng Town soup kitchen, and 377.43 yuan was spent on relief expenses. After deducting expenses, a balance of 184.59 yuan remains. The spring relief effort in the Fifth District has been completed, and the remaining funds are being sent to the Xinghua relief sub-association for accounting. A summary of the spring relief effort, a statement of income and expenses, and 42 ticket stubs totaling 3,420 tickets, as well as the sub-association's seal, are being submitted to the association for review."

Jisheng Society Co-Organizes Emergency Relief in Yixing 140

The Chinese Jisheng Society has repeatedly received reports from the Yixing Disaster Relief Committee in Jiangsu Province stating that the southwestern and southeastern regions of the county are surrounded by bare mountains with barren land, prone to drought and flooding. The area has suffered from recurring famines over the years. The area was flooded the year before last, and suffered from insect and drought disasters in the summer and autumn of last year. The harvests have been completely wiped out, which is unprecedented in decades. Villagers have chewed almost all of the fertilizer for the fertile fields and the grass that was cut for firewood, turning all of the mountains red and resulting in numerous suicides within families and deaths along the roads. Moreover, the mountain areas border Anhui and Zhejiang, attracting numerous bandits, causing merchants to hesitate and cutting off livelihoods, making the situation extremely precarious. Mr. Zhu Yuting, a local gentleman, has been appealing for help, but the funds obtained are far from sufficient. He urgently requests that benevolent aid be provided to relieve hunger and save lives. The suffering masses are eagerly awaiting help. The representative, Lawyer Sha Yankai, was sent to the society to appeal for help. The society has handled too many disaster areas in various provinces, and the relief funds are extremely difficult to raise, and the society's ability to assist is limited. However, the people are on the verge of death, and the society cannot bear to refuse them. Therefore, the society consulted with the Jiangsu Temporary Charity Relief Association to co-organize targeted relief efforts. Mr. Zhang Junzhongkuan has been publicly selected as the director of the Yixing relief effort, and he and fellow relief workers will depart for the county on June 23 to investigate and provide relief in the most severely affected areas.

The Family Dispute of Yan Juncai

Yan Juncai, a native of Yancheng, is currently over 50 years old. He previously ran a stationery store in his hometown and married Wang Chen, a widow, as his wife. Later, Yan lost his job and came to Shanghai to seek employment. He brought his daughter-in-law to Shanghai to work. Ten years have passed with no news. Yan is currently working as a tea server at a trade union at the North Railway Station. Wang Chen brought her son to Shanghai to find her. She ran into Yan at the intersection of Xinmin Road and Wuzhen Road in Zhabei the other day. Wang asked him about his daughter-in-law's whereabouts, and Yan prevaricated. Wang reported the matter to the police, and the police took him to the Fourth District First Precinct. After Director Yao interrogated him, he was sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for verification yesterday.

Free Talk

A Record of Three Islands 151

— Wang Yanjin

The first cry for gender equality: In today's Japan, the preference for males over females is like my country's Qing Dynasty. Women have absolutely no inheritance or political rights. The inequality between men and women is significant. However, women's education is gradually becoming popularized, and there are also many people who receive higher education. Therefore, the movement for political participation is becoming increasingly intense. However, women who have received higher education have repeatedly been rejected when they submit applications for the higher civil service examinations. This year, the authorities finally accepted one application. From now on, there will also be female prefectural governors in Japan (Japan is divided into three prefectures and forty-seven counties, and the prefectural governors are high-ranking civil servants directly under the central government). The applicant who was accepted this time is Ms. Tianbian Pingxue, the wife of Tokyo University of Technology Professor and Doctor of Engineering Tianbian Pingxue. Those in the know all call her Moeeinmaiden.

An unprecedented university strike: Kyoto Otani University has caused great controversy due to budget allocation issues. On the 11th of this month, all full-time or part-time professors and lecturers resigned, and clerks and other staff members also resigned en masse. When the student union received this report, it held a student assembly on the 12th and decided to collectively withdraw from the university. This is truly an unprecedented university strike in Japanese academic circles.

The Mohouluo of Mudu 152

— Yi Mei

Mudu is just a small town on the shores of Lake Tai. Since the Wu palace lady Xi Shi visited this place, it has made the cliffs and streams more beautiful, and the springs and rocks have gained luster. Her beautiful traces have been passed down for thousands of years. Therefore, on fine spring and autumn days, there is an endless stream of people punting here. Mudu produces water shield, which can dispel heat in summer and cold in autumn. Zeng Xiangxiang praised it as the first delicacy of Jiangdong. However, in addition to water shield, there is also a famous handicraft called Mohouluo. The Wu Men Biao Yin says that Mohouluo is produced in Mudu by the Yuan family. Yuan Yuchang of Mudu was skilled in sculpture and painting. The Mohouluo he created was especially exquisite. The Meng Hua Lu mentions that Yuan's descendants passed down his business for generations. More than ten years ago, there was still an earthen figure shop at the end of the west street in the town. It was exquisitely made and far surpassed the items from Huishan in Liangxi. People came from far and wide to purchase them. Unfortunately, the owner was old and had no heirs, and had no intention of continuing the business, so it closed. A relative of the Yue family lived in Mudu for generations. My wife also stayed there for a while and said that she had seen the Yue family's collection of ancient Mohouluo, numbering dozens of pieces, sculpting the characters in The Story of the Stone's Grand View Garden. All of them could express the infatuation of the Yihong Gongzi, the melancholy of the Xiaoxiang Concubine, the sharpness of Wang Xifeng, the honesty of Xiangyun, the handsomeness of Gongren, the simplicity of Xiangling, the intelligence of Zijuan, and the cleverness of Ping'er in their eyes. The skill was so divine that one was moved to stop and admire. The Mudu elder Yuan Xue'an, a painter, should be a descendant of Yu Chang. I do not know if he has any unique Mohouluo in his collection. I deeply wish to see it to broaden my horizons.

Let's Laugh it off Sea Trader

A: You've probably gained a few pounds

B: I've lost two pounds from the first half of the year.

A: Are you not well lately, that's why you've lost weight?

B: No, I haven't been sick. Probably because I took a bath yesterday.

Gentleman (picking up a silver dollar he dropped after a poor man went to pick it up): This dollar is mine! Why do you want to take it!

Poor man: This is clearly mine, why can't I pick it up!

Gentleman: What proof do you have?

Poor man: Look at the big hole in my pocket, that is proof that I dropped it.

Host: You said this chicken was a spring chicken, but why is it so old, it's like an old hen.

Cook: This chicken was probably hatched from an egg from the year before last.

A: Old Bing can be considered a very famous person in society.

B: Yes, his name is often in debt cases reported in the newspapers.

Wife: Dear, I had a good dream last night. I dreamed I was in heaven, and many fairies welcomed me. It was so happy.

Husband: Then why did you come back?

The sparrow craze as flood: In the past, small birds such as parrots, thrushes, and wagtails, as well as small yellow dogs, were shipped from Shanghai to the Japanese mainland, and were welcomed by the Japanese, who competed to buy them. The business was booming for a while. However, the number of people who like this is gradually decreasing. In this summer, the "mahjong" game, which has been popular for about two years, is exceptionally popular. People from all walks of life, whether in the business or academic world, are enjoying it. According to the Japanese customs authorities, the monthly import volume of mahjong tiles last year was only 50 to 60 sets. However, according to the Nagasaki Customs report for May this year, there were 311 sets as baggage carried by passengers and 105 sets as goods imported with a small tax. The total of 416 sets is an unprecedented amount. The Japanese call it the "flood" period of mahjong imports.

A Record of Visiting a Rotary Printing Machine 153

By Tianxu Wosheng

The Shanghai Savings Bank recently purchased a rotary printing machine from abroad, costing over three hundred taels of silver. Its printing plate is made of a roll of cotton paper with a layer of glue, slightly sticky.

It is about half a point thick, eight and a half inches wide, and one hundred and sixty inches long. Both ends are connected with waxed cloth, mounted on wooden axes so it can be unrolled like a hand scroll onto an iron plate with a felt surface. The actual flat surface used is only fourteen inches. Each time a manuscript is written with duplicating ink, it is applied to the glued surface, reportedly capable of printing over one hundred and ninety copies. However, actual tests showed that it could not print beyond eighty copies. Generally, a manuscript can be applied two to three times, totaling over two hundred copies. After the glue surface absorbs the ink, it must be left for twenty-four hours before it can be reused. The ink penetrates deep into the pores and cannot be washed off with water, hence the use of a rotary roll for gradual unrolling and repetition. The bank had not used it for long before it had to replace a roll of the glue surface due to flaking and melting, rendering it unusable. Upon request, I took it back for experimentation. It melted at 90 degrees Fahrenheit, with a glycerol content as high as 85%. Upon inquiring about the price from the Old Jinson Foreign Firm, each roll of glue board costs $55.40, and each bottle of ink costs $4.50, with a volume of only one English ounce and a high acetic acid content. I tried to imitate the ink with equal concentration, and it could print up to one hundred copies and be reprinted four times, so each manuscript can be printed more than four hundred copies. The cost is less than one yuan. The experimental glue board, with reduced glycerol and added protein, has a melting point up to 104 degrees Fahrenheit without the problems of water leakage and easy melting, since the hottest weather is only about 100 degrees Fahrenheit. After printing, it can be washed off immediately with water. If not washed off, after 24 hours, the ink will penetrate deep into the pores and not remain on the surface, ready for another manuscript to be applied and printed. Therefore, why necessarily use a rotary roll that makes the glue surface prone to damage? In my opinion, it is better to have multiple flat glue boards for replacement, which is sufficient. As for the machine, it is not particularly necessary. Its only advantage is printing ruled paper. In reality, when applying the manuscript, simply align the paper tightly with the corners of the glue board's edge and apply ink to the glue surface. Afterwards, when printing, place the paper in the original position according to the right angle, which can also print ruled paper without any skewing or misalignment. Why use this cumbersome iron machine? And since the glue board can be washed, two pieces are sufficient for turnover. If a manuscript is applied twice and printed by two people simultaneously, over two hundred copies can be printed in ten minutes. Washing off the floating ink and reprinting takes only ten more minutes. Therefore, I have modified this protein glue and acetic acid ink for use in our brand's printing equipment, which will be advertised later to avoid occupying this space. However, I have one thought about these printing tools: regarding culture, they are not luxuries, but imported goods are priced high, making them unaffordable for ordinary people, and using accessories becomes a source of endless profit. In this era of rising gold prices, those who purchase foreign machines inevitably have to purchase parts and consumables from abroad, and the suffering of being bound is immense. Is the lack of social trust in domestic products due to their low value, thus suspecting that their effectiveness must be inferior? Such psychological effects are truly the way our country becomes poor, which is lamentable.

Travels in Nanyang (37) 154

— Lianhua

On the fourth day, I visited the Japanese seaside fishing pavilion. The method involves setting up a wooden shed by the sea, building a cool pavilion, and providing tea and coffee to wait for tourists. Various types of fish are raised for guests to fish. If a guest catches a fish, they cannot take it but must give the pavilion several corners of a currency unit. Taking a fish is even more expensive. This is used for amusement. But operating this business is also a way to make money. Many white men and women come to play and fish. But the Japanese maids who serve tea are very old and dark, far inferior to the maids in Japan. Is this because they have become darker in Nanyang?

I heard that there are not many Japanese people in this area, less than a thousand. Most of them engage in the fishing industry. Fishing is a very profitable industry in the ocean. In the past, a friend wanted to start the South Pole Shipbuilding Company. According to his plan, the coastal fishing industry from Hainan to Niuzhuang would be very profitable. Only by placing electric lights on the fishing boats could one earn a profit of 10,000 yuan per day, it was said. It is a pity that his ship was not built. Nowadays, the Japanese are very powerful in the fishing industry in various places. Even the fish eaten in Shanghai, Nanjing, and other places are often called Japanese fish, as can be seen. The Japanese custom is to hang large paper carp in front of the door or on the roof of the house. Now, this custom can still be seen in the homes of Japanese people here. I once asked a Japanese woman in Japan what the meaning of hanging carp was. She replied that it meant wishing for a son because carp are brave and powerful. There are Japanese grocery stores, hotels, and barbershops here. One day, I wanted to get a haircut, but I did not want to go into a Japanese store. From my ideal of a "Great Unity," and not wanting to get a haircut in a Japanese store, it can be seen that national boundaries cannot be removed in a day, and the competition between ethnic groups cannot be avoided by anyone.

The fifth day was the Lunar Qingming Festival. Overseas, there is still the custom of the lunar calendar. Monks held a memorial service. I found the wording of the release ritual very tragic.

Chao Miao was a lyricist who understood Buddhism and wrote it, and reading it was very touching. The Qingming Festival is considered a ghost festival, as an old poem says, "On Qingming, no traveler does not miss home," so many men and women go to temples to pay respects and offer incense. Overseas, it is still the same as the customs in the country. I remember that during the spring, the Annam Daily was describing the grand occasion of the Lantern Festival in January. Also, the Spring Couplets posted by each family still use the old calendar, and fortune-telling and divination are entirely consistent. The business of treating illnesses is very prosperous, and some monks have become rich by engaging in this, which can also reveal the customs of overseas. Many doors are inscribed with the names of great immortals who treat illnesses. Next to a temple, a sign is written, "The Position of the Thousand-Year-Old Fox." In each temple, there is a method that can inspire people's faith: setting up memorial tablets for people's ancestors, in different sizes depending on the amount of money paid, from a thousand yuan, five hundred yuan, to fifty yuan, like spirit tablets, which are offered incense diligently by monks three times a day. This method is very popular in Japan, where people worship spirit tablets on behalf of others as if they were their own descendants. I think this method is quite reasonable. If the dead are conscious, they do not need to wait for their descendants to make offerings. This method is also feasible.

Re-printing is also time-consuming, but it only takes ten minutes, which is enough. Therefore, this protein glue and acetic acid ink have been modified for use in our brand's printing equipment, and advertisements will be published separately to avoid taking up this space. However, I have one thought about this: such printing equipment is not a luxury related to culture, but imported goods are priced high, making them unaffordable for ordinary people. Furthermore, accessories are a continuous source of profit. In this era of rising gold prices, those who purchase foreign machines inevitably have to purchase parts and consumables from abroad, and the suffering of being bound is immense. Is the lack of social trust in domestic products due to their low value, thus suspecting that their effectiveness must be inferior? Such psychological effects are truly the way our country becomes poor, which is lamentable.

Small Words on Pen Hooks 155

— Qiulang

The pen is one of the four treasures of the study, used for writing [according to Ancient and Modern Notes, in ancient times, bamboo and wooden slips were used, and pens were knives and awls; Meng Tian of the Qin Dynasty first used deer and sheep hair to make them]. Recently, there are many types of pens, including brushes, pencils, fountain pens, chalk, and stone pencils, each suited to its needs and all serving as beneficial tools for education and culture. However, the brush was created exclusively by our country, and the others are imitations of Western products. Therefore, the vast majority of people in society still use brushes when writing.

I once heard that a Westerner, upon returning to his country, described our country's brush to the public, saying, "The Chinese pen is a thin stick with a tuft of hair," which was considered strange and laughed at. In fact, things that have not been seen before are often considered strange upon first sight, just as our people initially viewed fountain pens and the like.

Zhang Jingzhao's beautiful eyebrow-drawing traces have been passed down as an eternal story. Therefore, the eyebrow-drawing pen should be considered the most successful of pens. But those ignorant children who practice calligraphy scribble at will, and fortune-tellers on the street sweep wildly with their pens – this is truly the misfortune of the pen. (A smile from the author.)

Alas, I have failed in both reading and business, and I am ashamed of my lack of success. I cannot emulate Ban Chao's discarding his pen to join the army, nor can I follow Lu Ji's abandoning his pen and burning his inkstone. I dare not even talk about Cao Cao's using two pens simultaneously. All I have is holding a pen to express my sorrow and wielding a brush to leave regrets, only earning a bald pen to spend my days. It is regrettable.

East Tour Correspondence (8) 156

— Wu Xiaohou

The current situation of social undertakings in Tokyo City, in Tokyo, as a source of culture and learning, takes active and implementing social policies when Tokyo Prefecture operations and private operations began to change, there was the establishment of nurseries, until 1890 when the municipal operations were changed until 1911, followed by the establishment of medical hospitals and employment agencies, etc. In 1919, due to the rice riots case, it wasn't until 1920 that the Tokyo Municipal Social Bureau was established. At the same time, the establishment of various social undertakings and the investigation and research of social conditions began to have concrete plans for implementation. Now, I will explain it by item:

(1) Approximate budget: The regular budget used by Tokyo City for social undertakings in the fourth year of Showa (1929) was 1,369,064 yuan, the temporary budget was 1,318,861 yuan, and the special accounting was 3,879,866 yuan, totaling approximately 6.5 million yuan.

(2) Social Welfare Committee System: According to statistics, there are approximately 300,000 poor, elderly, and sick people in Tokyo who need relief. For these 300,000 poor, elderly, and sick citizens, it is necessary to have a specialized and responsible organization under the municipal social bureau in each district to control the protection, guidance, and effective use of various social facilities in their daily lives. Therefore, the Social Welfare Committee system is established in each district. Among the 15 districts of Tokyo, the number of Social Welfare Committee members has been set up based on needs. There are 4 Social Welfare Committee members in Shitaya Ward, 6 Social Welfare Committee members each in Fukagawa, Asakusa, and Honjo Wards, 2 Social Welfare Committee members each in Kyobashi, Koishikawa, and Shiba Wards, and 1 Social Welfare Committee member each in Yotsuya, Hongo, Azabu, and Ushigome Wards. In total, there are 32 Social Welfare Committee members in the above 11 wards. Each Social Welfare Committee member averages 15 members, establishing a Social Welfare Committee office and setting up a chairman and vice-chairman each, entrusted by the mayor and the social bureau or ward chief to handle all social undertakings within the scope of their jurisdiction.

(3) Child Protection Facilities: Children are the foundation of healthy citizens in the future, and their protection is very important. There are five protection facilities: 1. Maternity hospitals and nurseries: There are three municipal ones, exclusively for poor people to give birth and raise infants. 2. Daycare centers: There are ten municipal ones. This type of organization is different from kindergartens and is exclusively for working parents who cannot afford to care for their four- and five-year-old children. 3. Child Counseling Centers: There are nine municipal ones, exclusively for citizens' children to consult on treatment methods when they are sick. 4. Juvenile Rehabilitation and Protection Centers: There are two municipal ones. One is the Tokyo Nursery, Inokashira School, which specializes in rehabilitating the most problematic teenagers. The other is the Tokyo Juvenile Protection Center, which specializes in taking in ordinary children who are not educated. 5. Children's playgrounds, i.e., children's parks: There are a total of 52 in Tokyo City, with three belonging to the municipality.

(4) Neighborhood Protection Projects: Neighborhood protection projects are labor education projects and are a type of supplementary education. The Tokyo Neighborhood Protection Hall is located in Koishikawa Ward, covering an area of 1,500 tsubo. The building is a steel-framed, reinforced concrete structure with a basement, totaling four floors. The first floor has offices, consultation rooms, meeting rooms, social rooms, lecture halls, night duty rooms, and servant rooms. The second floor has classrooms, libraries, study rooms, rental offices, balconies, and projection rooms. The third floor has indoor sports rooms, lecture rooms, club lodging rooms, etc. There are also outdoor exercise fields, dance fields, and sumo wrestling fields.

(5) Employment Referral Services: There are 15 municipal employment referral offices, including the Central Employment Referral Office and the Shibaen Employment Referral Office, etc., which specialize in introducing clerks and maids. On average, they refer approximately 30,000 to 60,000 people each year. There are also 8 employment referral offices such as the Shinjuku Employment Referral Office and the Hongo Employment Referral Office, which specialize in introducing labor services, totaling approximately 1.3 million people each year. There are also 5 municipal industrial training centers, which are exclusively for unemployed people to learn a profession, and their nature is different from the aforementioned employment referral offices.

Commercial News and Finance

Gold Standard Suffers a Reaction 157

Frequent False Alarms Depress the Market Yesterday, the gold standard situation on the 26th was complex and varied, with unpredictable ups and downs. The bizarre and chaotic state was unfathomable, but the downward trend was reversed. Throughout the day, there were eight taels of ups and downs. The foreign exchange market seemed to be loosening slightly, and the selling sentiment among peers was strong. Fuchang, Hengxing, Zhifeng, Yongyan, and Yu, and other firms generally sold short positions, while Yuanxing, Yonghan, Hengchun, Fayong, and retail investors bought in. From the early market's sudden surge, it immediately weakened, and later fluctuated by two or three taels. At noon, the sellers acted bravely, and the exchange rate also declined, resulting in a sharp drop of six taels. In the strong aftermarket, Zhifeng, Yongtaixing, Yuancheng, Yong, and other firms all bought in, while Wanxing, Taiheng Yuan, and others sold. Initially, due to weak market sentiment, it felt even more depressed, and suddenly fell to 611 taels. The foreign exchange market seemed to be strong, and the market buyers flourished, surging five or six taels. However, the market changes were impermanent, and the waves were endless. Finally, head-to-head investors came to sell, eagerly driving the price down sharply by five or six taels. In fact, it was repeatedly erratic, and peers seemed like blind people and lame horses, with an unclear path. As a result, it closed at just over 612 taels. Yesterday, the large silver bar recovered by one-eighth, and the silver price also increased by one-quarter.

The early market has declined steadily. The opening price of gold for August was 617 taels and 8 mace, a decrease of 4 taels and 3 mace. The gross market fluctuated by two or three taels, reaching 19 taels and 5 candareens. When the first official price was announced, it increased from 16 taels and 6 or 7 candareens to 18 taels and 6 candareens. Because the listed price did not change, it seemed slightly stable. Internally, it was average. Sumitomo bought September futures at 5 pence and 9375, and also absorbed October US dollars at 36 yuan and 4375. At 9:30, it was 17 taels and 3 candareens. More than ten minutes later, it increased to around 19 taels. After 10 o'clock, it gradually went downstream as the first exchange rate hardened. The Difficulties of the Japanese Cotton Industry 164

The Japanese cotton industry is facing difficulties for several reasons: first, the sharp decline in silver ingots has led to sluggish exports to China; second, the increase in Indian taxes has hindered exports; and third, the domestic implementation of austerity policies has reduced consumer spending. Furthermore, the decline in raw cotton prices has resulted in intangible losses from stockpiled inventory. Due to these factors, the Japanese cotton industry is experiencing a significant impact and is in a difficult situation. However, despite this environment and during the first period of reduced operations, the number of spindles in operation continues to increase, and cotton yarn production has consequently increased rather than decreased. The situation for this year is recorded below:

Number of Spindles Production Amount Number of Spindles Production Amount

January 6,390,000 231,000 March 5,960,000 219,000

February 6,230,000 234,000 April 5,962,000 227,000

From the table above, the number of spindles decreased by 260,000 and production decreased by 15,000 bales in February and March due to reduced operations. However, production increased again in April, which is quite strange. However, after considering the situation, the mills have their own difficulties. Small and medium-sized spinning mills, due to credit relationships with financial institutions, continue to produce despite knowing they are incurring losses. Large spinning mills, fearing social criticism due to worker unemployment, also reluctantly continue production despite knowing they are incurring losses. Engaging in production without being able to expand sales further exacerbates the difficulties. Participating in the spinning industry association and facing fierce criticism without being able to explain themselves, this decision led to a second round of 10% reduction in operations.

Grain: Flour Mills Reduce Prices

Yesterday, the flour market fell across the board in the morning and afternoon trading for all months. This is because current market sentiment has shifted its focus due to sluggish sales. The new wheat crop will inevitably be cheaper at some point, regardless of its quality. This fundamental factor suggests a potential decline. Furthermore, the northern provinces, due to a good wheat harvest, currently have no demand for Shanghai flour. With sluggish sales, the market inevitably declined. Millers again released large quantities, and large-scale speculative buyers also sold aggressively. Considering this, it is possible that prices may return to 4 cents and a half. As a result, the current month was down another 1.5 fen compared to the previous day, July was down 2 fen, August was down 2.5 fen, September was down 2.5 fen, October was down 1.5 fen, and November was down 2 fen.

Book Review

The Nationality and Internationality of Art 171

— Bing

By Ye Qiuyuan, Collection of Art Essays

Published by the United Bookstore

At a time when the literary movement of nationalism is thundering across the Chinese literary scene, I think it would be meaningful to introduce this book, [The Nationality and Internationality of Art], to our readers.

This book is divided into three parts: Part 1, Art Theory; Part 2, Literary Theory; and Part 3, Art History Theory. To save time and space, this article will only introduce Part 1, Art Theory, which is closely related to nationalist literature. The remaining two parts will have to wait until another opportunity.

Art Theory is a collection of six short art essays. His argument can be said to be a rising force in the current Chinese art scene, which is extremely shaken in thought and trapped in abnormal development.

The author is also unable to bear the decline of the Chinese art scene, so he said: [In order to make our art world gradually move towards a healthy development path, I feel that it is really no longer possible to wait any longer to say a few words today, knowing that in this era of great upheaval (or unable to understand a slightly more serious theory] (page 39). Although we also feel that in this era of great upheaval, many people are like drunkards, with blurred eyes and unable to distinguish right from wrong, relying on a burst of drunken enthusiasm to shout and jump around. If you don't understand reason and try to talk to him politely, it will of course be a waste of time and he won't listen to a single word. If you're not careful, he will also treat you unkindly with malice. Smart people are not very willing to do such unpleasant things, but we can't allow a drunkard to do whatever he wants, which is also inevitable. If everyone stands by with their hands in their sleeves, everything will inevitably be destroyed in the drunkard's hands. This is also the case in the current art world. We feel that the more turbulent the era, the more we need serious theories, and the responsibility of artists will be increased. We must not allow art to be smoked out by a group of drunkards and destroyed.

Here we know that the author is loyal to art, so he finally cannot remain silent. At the same time, we can also see his views on art, the current state of the Chinese art world, and the common efforts that the art world should make in the future.

In the chapter on the main trends of modern art, he explained the nature, distribution, and development of modernism. In the meaning of art, he discussed the essence of art, the classification of art, and the origin of art one by one, and then proposed the spirit of new art. He said that the spirit of modern art is movement and originality. Finally, he quoted Mr. Zhu Yingpeng's words to conclude that the new art movement at least contains full secular thought and full free thought, at least to attack ideological thought, to attack religious thought, to attack mountain and forest hermit thought, to attack fate thought, to attack wind-chanting and moon-playing, red-dressed men and green-dressed women literature]. The author highly agrees with this view, so he also hopes to have considerable construction and considerable creation.

The author believes that art cannot be separated from politics. He uses historical facts to prove his theory that [art cannot be separated from politics and art evolves with politics] and that the development of national art must be filled with national concepts.

In the chapter on the nationality and internationality of art, the author further recognizes that modern politics is completely dominated by nationalism and internationalism. These two trends seem to be incompatible, but they have a very close cause-and-effect relationship. The more internationalized society becomes, the more obvious the color of nationalism becomes. If, under this trend of internationalization, one does not express one's own national characteristics, one will inevitably perish. Therefore, when art is internationalized, the nationality of art must be more prominent, so that the spirit of our nation can be fully expressed internationally to obtain the basis for our superior international position. In modern art and nationalism, the author explained the relationship between art and the nation more thoroughly. Now I will quote it below as the result of this article.

······Art will ultimately take the nation as its background, and the life of the nation is the subject matter expressed in artistic works. Art is national, and what Westerners call ＮＡtionalart, or national art or ethnic art, is based on folk life, folk thought, folk religion, and the Locialornationaltemqerment of the nation as its artistic purpose. This situation is obvious. Western artists engage in national art, taking the nation as the premise and making it their responsibility to promote the national style. This situation is not seen in China. Chinese people only have family style and family learning, but they lack national style and national life. Modern art is still a national or ethnic art, although this movement

seems to have affected various countries.

Correction: The author [Bing Hui] of the Avant-Garde Weekly Creative Issue introduced the other day was mistakenly identified as [Bing Heng]. We hereby correct this.

Guidelines for Book Review Manuscripts 172

(1) The text should be limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, and other books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books will not be introduced.

(2) Texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(4) Each text should not exceed 3,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write carelessly. Western text can be abbreviated as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.
